⟪ar-quote:أَمَرَهُ بِتَقْوَى اللهِ، وَإِيثَارِ طَاعَتِهِ، وَاتِّبَاعِ مَا أَمَرَ بِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ- مِنْ فَرَائِضِهِ وَسُنَنِهِ، الَّتِي لاَ يَسْعَدُ أَحَدٌ إِلاَّ بِاتِّبَاعِهَا، وَلاَ يَشْقَى إِلاَّ مَعَ جُحُودِهَا وَإِضَاعَتِهَا، وَأَنْ يَنْصُرَ اللهَ سُبْحَانَهُ بَيَدِهِ وَقَلْبِهِ وَلِسَانِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ، جَلَّ اسْمُهُ، قَدْ تَكَفَّلَ بِنَصْرِ مَنْ نَصَرَهُ، وَإِعْزَازِ مَنْ أَعَزَّهُ. وَأَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَكْسِرَ نَفْسَهُ عِنْدَ الشَّهَوَاتِ، وَيَزَعَهَا عِنْدَ الْجَمَحَاتِ، فَإِنَّ النَّفْسَ أَمَّارَةٌ بِالسُّوءِ، إِلاَّ مَا رَحِمَ اللهُ⟫

## The Qualifications of a Governor and His Responsibilities

Know, O Malik, that I have sent you to a region where successive administrations—both just and tyrannical—have held sway. The people now will scrutinize your conduct as you once examined that of your predecessors, and they will pass judgment upon you as you have judged them. The virtuous are known by the reputation that Allah circulates for them through the tongues of His creatures. Let the finest treasury you preserve be the treasury of righteous deeds. Master your passions and guard your soul from what is unlawful for you; for restraint of the self means holding it at the midpoint between what it desires and what it abhors.[^cite-12]

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ اعْلَمْ يَا مَالكُ، أَنِّي قدْ وَجَّهْتُكَ إِلَى بِلاَد قَدْ جَرَتْ عَلَيْهَا دُوَلٌ قَبْلَكَ، مِنْ عَدْل وَجَوْر، وَأَنَّ النَّاسَ يَنْظُرُونَ مِنْ أُمُورِكَ فِى مِثْلِ مَا كُنْتَ تَنْظُرُ فِيهِ مِنْ أُمُورِ الْوُلاَةِ قَبْلَكَ، وَيَقُولُونَ فِيكَ مَا كُنْتَ تَقُولُ فِيهِمْ،إِنَّمَا يُسْتَدَلُّ عَلَى الصَّالِحِينَ بِمَا يُجْرِي اللهُ لَهُمْ عَلَى أَلْسُنِ عِبَادِهِ. فَلْيَكُنْ أَحَبَّ الذَّخَائِرِ إِلَيْكَ ذَخِيرَةُ الْعَمَلِ الصَّالِحِ، فَامْلِكْ هَوَاكَ، وَشُحَّ بِنَفْسِكَ عَمَّا لاَ يَحِلُّ لَكَ، فَإِنَّ الشُّحَّ بِالنَّفْسِ الاْنْصَافُ مِنْهَا فَيَما أَحْبَبْتَ وَكَرِهْتَ⟫

Cultivate in your heart mercy for those under your charge, affection and kindness toward them. Do not stand over them as a voracious beast that devours them; they are of two kinds: either your brother in faith or your equal in creation. They will slip and encounter ailments; they act sometimes deliberately and sometimes through error. Extend to them your forgiveness and pardon as you would wish Allah to extend His pardon to you. For you stand above them, your responsible Commander stands above you, and Allah stands above him who appointed you. He has entrusted their affairs to your stewardship and tested you through them.[^cite-13]

⟪ar-quote:وَأَشْعِرْ قَلْبَكَ الرَّحْمَةَ لِلرَّعِيَّةِ، وَالْـمَحَبَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَاللُّطْفَ بِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَكُونَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ سَبُعاً ضَارِياً تَغْتَنِمُ أَكْلَهُمْ، فَإِنَّهُمْ صِنْفَانِ- إِمَّا أَخٌ لَكَ فِي الدِّينِ، وَإمّا نَظِيرٌ لَكَ فِي الْخَلْقِ، يَفْرُطُ مِنْهُمُ الزَّلَلُ، وَتَعْرِضُ لَهُمُ الْعِلَلُ،يُؤْتَى عَلَى أَيْدِيهِمْ فِي الَعَمْدِ وَالْخَطَاَ، فَأَعْطِهِمْ مِنْ عَفْوِكَ وَصَفْحِكَ مِثْلَ الَّذِي تُحِبُّ أَنْ يُعْطِيَكَ اللهُ مِنْ عَفْوِهِ وَصَفْحِهِ، فَإِنَّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ، وَ وَالِي الاْمْرِ عَلَيْكَ فَوْقَكَ، وَاللهُ فَوْقَ مَنْ وَلاَّكَ! وَقَدِ اسْتَكْفَاكَ أَمْرَهُمْ، وَابْتَلاَكَ بِهِمْ⟫

Do not set yourself in opposition to Allah, for you have no power against His might and cannot do without His pardon and mercy. Do not repent of clemency, nor exult in punishment. Do not hasten to strike in anger if you can find an escape. Do not say, "I have been given authority, I must be obeyed," for that breeds discord in the heart, weakens faith, and brings one near to ruin. Should your position produce in you pride or arrogance, look upon the greatness of Allah's dominion over you and His power—a power over you that you do not possess over yourself. This will curb your ambition, heal your haughtiness, and restore the wisdom that has escaped you.[^cite-14]

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تَنْصِبَنَّ نَفْسَكَ لِحَرْبِ اللهِ، فَإِنَّهْ لاَيَدَيْ لَكَ بِنِقْمَتِهِ، وَلاَ غِنَى بِكَ عَنْ عَفْوِهِ وَرَحْمَتِهِ. وَلاَ تَنْدَمَنَّ عَلَى عَفْو، وَلاَ تَبْجَحَنَّ بِعُقُوبَة، وَلاَ تُسْرِعَنَّ إِلَى بَادِرَة وَجَدْتَ مِنْهَا مَنْدُوحَةً، وَلاَ تَقُولَنَّ- إِنِّي مُؤَمَّرٌ آمُرُ فَأُطَاعُ، فَإِنَّ ذلِكَ إِدْغَالٌ فِي الْقَلْبِ، وَمَنْهَكَةٌ لِلدِّينِ، وَتَقَرُّبٌ مِنَ الْغِيَرِ. وَإِذَا أَحْدَثَ لَكَ مَا أَنْتَ فِيهِ مِنْ سُلْطَانِكَ أُبَّهَةً أَوْ مَخِيلَةً، فَانْظُرْ إِلَى عِظَمِ مُلْكِ اللهِ فَوْقَكَ، وَقُدْرَتِهِ مَنْكَ عَلَى مَا لاَ تَقْدرِ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ نَفْسِكَ، فَإِنَّ ذلِكَ يُطَامِنُ إِلَيْكَ مِنْ طِمَاحِكَ، وَيَكُفُّ عَنْكَ مِنْ غَرْبِكَ،يَفِيءُ إِلَيْكَ بِمَا عَزَبَ عَنْكَ مِنْ عَقْلِكَ⟫

Beware of equating yourself with Allah in His majesty or imitating Him in His sovereignty (*jabārūt*, absolute power), for Allah humbles every tyrant and disgraces every arrogant person.

⟪ar-quote:إِيَّاكَ وَمُسَامَاةَ اللهِ فِي عَظَمَتِهِ، وَالتَّشَبُّهَ بِهِ فِي جَبَرُوتِهِ، فَإِنَّ اللهَ يُذِلُّ كُلَّ جَبَّار، وَيُهِينُ كُلَّ مُخْتَال⟫

Be just with Allah and be just with the people against yourself, your family, and those of your subjects toward whom you have affection. For if you do not, you will be oppressive. When someone oppresses the creatures of Allah, Allah becomes his opponent instead of His creatures. When Allah is someone's opponent, He confounds his plea, and such a person remains at war with Allah until he desists and repents. Nothing more speedily reverses Allah's blessing or hastens His retribution than persistence in injustice, for Allah hears the prayer of the oppressed and lies in wait for the oppressor.[^cite-15]

⟪ar-quote:أَنْصِفِ اللهَ وَأَنْصِفِ النَّاسَ مِنْ نَفْسِكَ، وَمِنْ خَاصَّةِ أَهْلِكَ، وَمَنْ لَكَ فِيهِ هَوىً مِنْ رَعِيَّتِكَ، فَإِنَّكَ إِلاَّ تَفْعَلْ تَظْلِمْ، وَمَنْ ظَلَمَ عِبَادَ اللهِ كَانَ اللهُ خَصْمَهُ دُونَ عِبَادِهِ، وَمَنْ خَاصَمَهُ اللهُ أَدْحَضَ حُجَّتَهُ، وَكَانَ لله حَرْباً حَتَّى يَنْزعَ وَيَتُوبَ. وَلَيْسَ شَيْءٌ أَدْعَى إِلَى تَغْيِيرِ نِعْمَةِ اللهِ وَتَعْجِيلِ نِقْمَتِهِ مِنْ إِقَامَة عَلَى ظُلْم، فَإِنَّ اللهَ سَميِعٌ دَعْوَةَ الْمَظْلُومِينَ، وَهُوَ لِلظَّالِمِينَ بِالْمِرْصَادِ⟫

The course you should most desire is that which is most equitable in the matter of right, most universal in justice, and most comprehensive in securing the consent of those under you. For the displeasure of the common people erases the approval of the elite, while the displeasure of the elite is forgiven in the presence of the approval of the common people. Among your subjects, none are more burdensome to the governor in times of ease, less helpful in adversity, more averse to just treatment, more importunate in demanding favors, less grateful when given something, slower to accept excuses when refused, and weaker in endurance during hardship than the elite. The common people form the pillar of religion, the collective body of Muslims, and the defense against enemies. Let your inclination therefore turn toward them, and your attachment be with them.[^cite-16]

⟪ar-quote:كُنْ أَحَبَّ الاْمُورِ إِلَيْكَ أَوْسَطُهَا فِي الْحَقِّ، وَأَعَمُّهَا فِي الْعَدْلِ، وَأَجْمَعُهَا لِرِضَى الرَّعِيَّةِ، فَإِنَّ سُخْطَ الْعَامَّةِ يُجْحِفُ بِرِضَى الْخَاصَّةِ، وَإِنَّ سُخْطَ الْخَاصَّةِ يُغْتَفَرُ مَعَ رِضَى الْعَامَّةِ. وَلَيْسَ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الرَّعِيَّةِ، أَثْقَلَ عَلَى الْوَالِي مَؤُونَةً فِي الرَّخَاءِ، وَأَقَلَّ مَعُونَةً لَهُ فِي الْبَلاَءِ، وَأَكْرَهَ لِلاْنْصَافِ، وَأَسْأَلَ بِالاْلْحَافِ، وَأَقَلَّ شُكْراً عِنْدَ الاْعْطَاءِ، وَأَبْطَأَ عُذْراً عِنْدَ الْمَنْعِ، وَأَضْعَفَ صَبْراً عِنْدَ مُلِمَّاتِ الدَّهْرِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْخَاصَّةِ، وَإِنَّمَا عَمُودُ الدِّينِ، وَجِمَاعُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، وَالْعُدَّةُ لِلاْعْدَاءِ، الْعَامَّةُ مِنَ الاْمَّةِ، فَلْيَكُنْ صِغْوُكَ لَهُمْ، وَمَيْلُكَ مَعَهُمْ⟫

The one among those under your charge most distant from you and most detestable in your view should be he who is most zealous in ferreting out the faults of the people. For people do have faults, and the ruler is the most fit to conceal them. Do not expose what remains hidden from you, for your obligation is only to rectify what appears to you; Allah will judge what lies beyond your knowledge. Cover the faults so far as you are able; Allah will cover those of your faults that you wish hidden from your subjects. Untie every knot of hatred among the people and sever the cause of every enmity. Feign ignorance of what is unclear to you. Do not hasten to credit a slanderer, for the slanderer is a cheat despite his appearance as a well-wisher.[^cite-17]

⟪ar-quote:وَلْيَكُنْ أَبْعَدَ رَعِيَّتِكَ مِنْكَ، وَأشْنَأَهُمْ عِنْدَكَ، أَطْلَبُهُمْ لِمَعَائِبِ النَّاسِ، فإنَّ في النَّاسِ عُيُوباً، الْوَالِي أَحَقُّ مَنْ سَتَرَهَا، فَلاَ تَكْشِفَنَّ عَمَّا غَابَ عَنْكَ مِنْهَا، فَإنَّمَا عَلَيْكَ تَطْهِيرُ مَا ظَهَرَ لَكَ، وَاللهُ يَحْكُمُ عَلَى مَا غَابَ عَنْكَ، فَاسْتُرِ الْعَوْرَةَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتَ يَسْتُرِ اللهُ مِنْكَ ما تُحِبُّ سَتْرَهُ مِنْ رَعِيَّتِكَ. أَطْلِقْ عَنِ النَّاسِ عُقْدَةَ كُلِّ حِقْد، وَاقْطَعْ عَنْكَ سَبَبَ كُلِّ وِتْر، وَتَغَابَ عَنْ كلِّ مَا لاَ يَضِحُ لَكَ، وَلاَ تَعْجَلَنَّ إِلَى تَصْدِيقِ سَاع، فَإِنَّ السَّاعِيَ غَاشٌ،⟫

Do not include among your counselors a miser who would discourage you from generosity and warn you of poverty, nor a coward who would weaken your affairs, nor a rapacious person who would make attractive to you the accumulation of wealth through injustice. For stinginess, cowardice, and avarice are diverse dispositions unified by a bad opinion of Allah.

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تُدْخِلَنَّ فِي مَشُورَتِكَ بَخِيلاً يَعْدِلُ بِكَ عَنِ الْفَضْلِ، وَيَعِدُكَ الْفَقْرَ، وَلاَ جَبَاناً يُضعِّفُكَ عَنِ الاْمُورِ، وَلاَ حَرِيصاً يُزَيِّنُ لَكَ الشَّرَهَ بِالْجَوْرِ، فَإِنَّ الْبُخْلَ وَالْجُبْنَ وَالْحِرْصَ غَرَائِزُ شَتَّى يَجْمَعُهَا سُوءُ الظَّنِّ بِاللهِ⟫

The worst minister is one who previously served the wicked before you and who shared in their sins. Do not make such a one your intimate counselor, for they are abettors of the sinful and brothers of the unjust. You can find worthy alternatives—those who share their views and influence but not their sins and vices, who have never aided an oppressor in his oppression or a sinner in his transgression. These will cause you less burden and provide better support; they will be most considerate of you and least attached to others. Make them your intimate companions in both privacy and public affairs.[^cite-18]

⟪ar-quote:شَرُّ وُزَرَائِكَ مَنْ كَانَ لِلاْشْرَارِ قَبْلَكَ وَزِيراً، وَمَنْ شَرِكَهُمْ فِي الاْثَامِ، فَلاَ يَكُونَنَّ لَكَ بِطَانَةً، فَإِنَّهُمْ أَعْوَانُ الاْثَمَةِ، وَإِخْوَانُ الظَّلَمَةِ، وَأَنْتَ وَاجِدٌ مِنْهُمْ خَيْرَ الْخَلَفِ مِمَّنْ لَهُ مِثْلُ آرَائِهِمْ وَنَفَاذِهِمْ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ مِثْلُ آصَارِهِمْ وَأَوْزَارِهِمْ وَ آثَامِهِمْ، مِمَّنْ لَمْ يُعَاوِنْ ظَالِماً عَلَى ظُلْمِهِ، وَلاَ آثِماً عَلَى إِثْمِهِ، أُولئِكَ أَخَفُّ عَلَيْكَ مَؤُونَةً، وَأَحْسَنُ لَكَ مَعُونَةً، وَأَحْنَى عَلَيْكَ عَطْفاً، وَأَقَلُّ لِغَيْرِكَ إِلْفاً، فَاتَّخِذْ أُولئِكَ خَاصَّةً لِخَلَوَاتِكَ وَحَفَلاَتِكَ⟫

Among them, let those be most favored by you who speak truth to your face, however bitter, and who support you least in actions that Allah dislikes in His friends—even if such actions accord with your desires. Cleave to the pious and truthful; train them not to flatter you nor praise you falsely for deeds you have not performed. For excessive flattery breeds vanity and approaches haughtiness.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ لْيَكُنْ آثَرُهُمْ عِنْدَكَ أَقْوَلَهُمْ بِمُرِّ الْحَقِّ لَكَ، وأَقَلَّهُمْ مُسَاعَدَةً فِيَما يَكُونُ مِنْكَ مِمَّا كَرِهَ اللهُ لاِوْلِيَائِهِ، وَاقِعاً ذلِكَ مِنْ هَوَاكَ حَيْثُ وَقَعَ. وَالْصَقْ بِأَهْلِ الْوَرَعِ وَالصِّدْقِ، ثُمَّ رُضْهُمْ عَلَى أَلاَّ يُطْرُوكَ وَلاَ يُبَجِّحُوكَ بِبَاطِل لَمْ تَفْعَلْهُ، فَإِنَّ كَثْرَةَ الاْطْرَاءِ تُحْدِثُ الزَّهْوَ، وَتُدْنِي مِنَ الْعِزَّةِ⟫

Let not the virtuous and the vicious hold equal station before you, for to do so discourages the virtuous from virtue and encourages the vicious to vice. Fix each in the position that befits him. Know that nothing better establishes a ruler's good standing with his subjects than benevolence toward them, relief of their hardships, and refraining from imposing unbearable burdens upon them. Conduct yourself in this manner so as to earn a good reputation among your subjects; such esteem relieves you of great anxieties. The one most entitled to your favorable regard is he whom you have treated well, and the one most entitled to your disfavor is he whom you have treated badly.[^cite-19]

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ يَكُونَنَّ الْـمُحْسِنُ وَالْمُسِيءُ عِنْدَكَ بِمَنْزِلَة سَوَاء، فَإِنَّ فِي ذلِكَ تَزْهِيداً لاِهْلِ الاْحْسَانِ فِي الاْحْسَانِ،تَدْرِيباً لاِهْلِ الاْسَاءَةِ عَلَى الاْسَاءَةِ، وَأَلْزِمْ كُلاًّ مِنْهُمْ مَا أَلْزَمَ نَفْسَهُ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ شَيْءٌ بِأَدْعَى إِلَى حُسْنِ ظَنِّ وَال بِرَعِيَّتِهِ مِنْ إحْسَانِهِ إِلَيْهِمْ، وَتَخْفِيفِهِ الْمَؤُونَاتِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَتَرْكِ اسْتِكْرَاهِهِ إِيَّاهُمْ عَلَى مَا لَيْسَ لهُ قِبَلَهُمْ، فَلْيَكُنْ مِنْكَ فِي ذلِكَ أَمْرٌ يَجَتَمِعُ لَكَ بِهِ حُسْنُ الظَّنِّ بِرَعِيَّتِكَ، فَإِنَّ حُسْنَ الظَّنِّ يَقْطَعُ عَنْكَ نَصْباً طَوِيلاً، وَإِنَّ أَحَقَّ مَنْ حَسُنَ ظَنُّكَ بِهِ لَمَنْ حَسُنَ بَلاَؤُكَ عِنْدَهُ، وَإِنَّ أَحَقَّ مَنْ سَاءَ ظَنُّكَ بِهِ لَمَنْ سَاءَ بَلاَؤُكَ عِنْدَهُ⟫

Do not abandon the good customs established by the righteous leaders of this community, through which unity was achieved and the people prospered. Introduce no innovation that would injure these earlier practices, lest those who instituted them receive the reward while you bear the burden of having reversed them. Increase your consultation with the learned and discussions with the wise to consolidate the prosperity of your realm and maintain that which your predecessors established.[^cite-20]

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ تَنْقُضْ سُنَّةً صَالِحَةً عَمِلَ بِهَا صُدُورُ هذِهِ الاْمَّةِ، وَاجْتَمَعتْ بِهَا الاْلْفَةُ، وَصَلَحَتْ عَلَيْهَا الرَّعِيَّةُ،لاَ تُحْدِثَنَّ سُنَّةً تَضُرُّ بِشَيء مِنْ مَاضِي تِلْكَ السُّنَنِ، فَيَكُونَ الاْجْرُ بِمَنْ سَنَّهَا، وَالْوِزْرُ عَلَيْكَ بِمَا نَقَضْتَ مِنْهَا. وَأَكْثِرْ مُدَارَسَةَ الَعُلَمَاءِ، وَمُنَافَثَةَ الْحُكَمَاءِ، فِي تَثْبِيتِ مَا صَلَحَ عَلَيْهِ أَمْرُ بِلاَدِكَ،⟫

Understand that the people consist of classes interdependent upon one another, each unable to do without the other. Among them are the soldiers of Allah; the secretaries of the general and particular affairs; the judges administering justice; the administrators of equity and clemency; those who pay the poll tax (*jizyah*) and land tax (*kharāj*) from the protected unbelievers and believing peoples; the merchants and artisans; and finally, the destitute and needy class. Allah has assigned to each their portion and prescribed their boundaries in His Book and the Sunnah of His Prophet—a covenant preserved with us.[^cite-21]

⟪ar-quote:وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الرَّعِيَّةَ طَبَقَاتٌ لاَ يَصْلُحُ بَعْضُهَا إلاَّ بِبَعْض، وَلاَ غِنَى بِبَعْضِهَا عَنْ بَعْض- فَمِنْهَا جُنُودُ اللهِ،مِنْهَا كُتَّابُ الْعَامَّةِ وَالْخَاصَّةِ، وَمِنْهَا قُضَاةُ الْعَدْلِ، وَمِنهَا عُمَّالُ الاْنْصَافِ وَالرِّفْقِ، وَمِنْهَا أَهْلُ الْجِزْيَةِ وَالْخَراجِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الذِّمَّةِ وَمُسْلِمَةِ النَّاسِ، وَمِنْهَا التُّجَّارُ وَأَهْلُ الصِّنَاعَاتِ، وَمِنهَا الطَّبَقَةُ السُّفْلَى مِنْ ذَوِي الْحَاجَةِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ، وَكُلٌّ قَدْ سَمَّى اللهُ سَهْمَهُ، وَوَضَعَ عَلَى حَدِّهِ وَفَرِيضَتِهِ فِي كِتَابِهِ أَوْ سُنَّةِ نَبِيِّهِ (صلى الله عليه وآله)عَهْداً مِنْهُ عِنْدَنَا مَحْفُوظاً⟫

The soldiers are, by Allah's will, the fortress of the subjects, the adornment of the ruler, the glory of the faith, and the means of security. The subjects cannot endure without them. Yet the soldiers themselves subsist only through the revenues that Allah has ordained, which furnish them the strength to wage war, afford them livelihood, and supply their needs. These two classes cannot stand without the third: the judges, administrators, and secretaries who establish contracts, gather revenues, and are trusted with both general and particular matters.

⟪ar-quote:فَالْجُنُودُ، بِإِذْنِ اللهِ، حُصُونُ الرَّعِيَّةِ، وَزَيْنُ الْوُلاَةِ، وعِزُّ الدِّينِ، وَسُبُلُ الاْمْنِ، وَلَيْسَ تَقُومُ الرَّعِيَّةُ إِلاَّ بِهِمْ. ثُمَّ لاَ قِوَامَ لِلْجُنُودِ إِلاَّ بِمَا يُخْرِجُ اللهُ لَهُمْ مِنَ الْخَرَاجِ الَّذِي يَقْوَوْنَ بِهِ فِي جِهَادِ عَدُوِهِمْ، وَيَعْتَمِدُونَ عَلَيْهِ فِيَما أصْلَحهُمْ، وَيَكُونُ مِنْ وَرَاءِ حَاجَتِهِمْ. ثُمَّ لاَ قِوَامَ لِهذَيْنِ الصِّنْفَيْنِ إِلاَّ بِالصِّنْفِ الثَّالِثِ مِنَ الْقُضَاةِ وَالْعُمَّالِ وَالْكُتَّابِ، لِمَا يُحْكِمُونَ مِنَ الْمَعَاقِدِ، وَيَجْمَعُونَ مِنَ الْمَنَافِعِ، وَيُؤْتَمَنُونَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ خَوَاصِّ الاْمُورِ وَعَوَامِّهَا⟫

All these classes depend in turn upon the traders and artisans, who supply their necessities, establish markets, and spare them from having to gather supplies by their own hands. Finally, there is the lowest class of the needy and destitute, to whom assistance and support are obligatory. In Allah's bounty there is sufficiency for all, and to each the ruler owes a right according to what serves their welfare. The ruler cannot acquit himself of the obligations Allah has laid upon him in this regard except through striving and seeking Allah's aid, establishing himself in the pursuit of right, and enduring with patience whatever is light or difficult.[^cite-22]

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ قِوَامَ لَهُمْ جَمِيعاً إِلاَّ بِالتُّجَّارِ وَذَوِي الصِّنَاعَاتِ، فِيَما يَجْتَمِعُونَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ مَرَافِقِهِمْ، وَيُقِيمُونَهُ مِنْ أَسْوَاقِهِمْ، وَيَكْفُونَهُمْ مِنَ التَّرَفُّقِ بِأَيْدِيهِمْ ممّا لاَ يَبْلُغُهُ رِفْقُ غَيْرِهِمْ. ثُمَّ الطَّبَقَةُ السُّفْلَى مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَاجَةِ وَالْمَسْكَنَةِ الَّذِينَ يَحِقُّ رِفْدُهُمْ وَمَعُونَتُهُمْ. وَفِي اللهِ لِكُلّ سَعَةٌ، وَلِكُلٍّ عَلَى الْوَالِي حَقٌ بِقَدْرِ مَا يُصْلِحُهُ. وَلَيْسَ يَخْرُجُ الْوَالِي مِنْ حَقِيقَةِ مَا أَلْزَمَهُ اللهُ مِنْ ذلِكَ إِلاَّ بِالاْهْتِمامِ وَالاسْتِعَانَةِ بِاللهِ، وَتَوْطِينِ نَفْسِهِ عَلَى لُزُومِ الْحَقِّ، وَالصَّبْرِ عَلَيْهِ فِيَما خَفَّ عَلَيْهِ أَوْ ثَقُلَ⟫

## The Army

Entrust command of your forces to the man who, in your estimation, is most sincere in his counsel to Allah, His Prophet, and your Imam; who possesses the purest heart and greatest forbearance—one slow to anger, ready to accept excuses, merciful to the weak, stern toward the strong; whose valor is not aroused by violence nor whose energy diminished by weakness.[^cite-23]

⟪ar-quote:فَوَلِّ مِنْ جُنُودِكَ أَنْصَحَهُمْ فِي نَفْسِكَ لله وَلِرَسُولِهِ وَلاِمَامِكَ، وَأَنْقَاهُمْ جَيْباً، وَأَفْضَلَهُمْ حِلْماً مِمَّنْ يُبْطِىءُ عَنِ الْغَضَبِ، وَيَسْتَرِيحُ إِلَى الْعُذْرِ، وَيَرْأَفُ بِالضُّعَفَاءِ، وَيَنْبُو عَلَى الاْقْوِيَاءِ، وَمِمَّنْ لاَ يُثِيرُهُ الْعُنْفُ، وَلاَ يَقْعُدُ بِهِ الضَّعْفُ⟫

Surround yourself with men of noble descent and worthy houses, of good repute and upright conduct. Then associate with the valiant, the brave, the generous, and the benevolent, for these embody honor and are repositories of virtue. Attend to their circumstances as parents attend to their children. Do not regard any provision you make to strengthen them as excessive, nor any kindness you extend as negligible, however small; for such solicitude inclines them toward sincerity and creates in them a good opinion of you. Do not neglect their minor concerns by relying solely on attending to their major ones, for both their small favors and their substantial support serve necessary purposes.[^cite-24]

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ الْصَقْ بَذَوِي الْمُرُوءَاتِ وَالاْحْسَابِ، وَأَهْلِ الْبُيُوتَاتِ الصَّالِحَةِ، وَالسَّوَابِقِ الْحَسَنَةِ، ثُمَّ أَهْلِ النَّجْدَةِ وَالشَّجَاعَةِ، وَالسَّخَاءِ وَالسَّماحَةِ، فَإِنَّهُمْ جِمَاعٌ مِنَ الْكَرَمِ، وَشُعَبٌ مِنَ الْعُرْفِ. ثُمَّ تَفَقَّدْ مِنْ أُمُورِهِمْ مَا يَتَفَقَّدُهُ الْوَالِدَانِ مِنْ وَلَدِهِمَا، وَلاَ يَتَفَاقَمَنَّ فِي نَفْسِكَ شَيْءٌ قَوَّيْتَهُمْ بِهِ، وَلاَ تَحْقِرَنَّ لُطْفاً تَعَاهَدْتَهُمْ بِهِ وَإِنْ قَلَّ، فَإِنَّهُ دَاعِيَةٌ لَهُمْ إِلَى بَذْلِ النَّصِيحَةِ لَكَ، وَحُسْنِ الظَّنِّ بِكَ. وَلاَ تَدَعْ تَفَقُّدَ لَطيِفِ أُمُورِهِمُ اتِّكَالاً عَلَى جَسِيمِهَا، فَإِنَّ لِلْيَسِيرِ مِنْ لُطْفِكَ مَوْضِعاً يَنْتَفِعُونَ بِهِ، وَلِلْجَسِيمِ مَوْقِعاً لاَ يَسْتَغْنُونَ عَنْهُ.⟫

Let the commander of your forces occupy such a position that he aids them equitably and bestows upon them and their families from his own resources such that their sole worry becomes the confrontation with the enemy. Your kindness toward them will turn their hearts toward you. The most gratifying condition for rulers is the establishment of justice in their lands and the manifestation of their subjects' affection. Yet subjects' love manifests itself only through purity of heart, and their sincerity proves itself only through vigilance toward their commanders. Do not burden them with the weight of their offices, nor do you begrudge the passage of their terms. Be generous in your expectations of them and persistent in your praise of them; recount the noble deeds of those who have distinguished themselves, for the mention of virtuous actions stirs the brave and incites the reluctant, if Allah wills.[^cite-25]

⟪ar-quote:وَلْيَكُنْ آثَرُ رُؤوسِ جُنْدِكَ عِنْدَكَ مَنْ وَاسَاهُمْ فِي مَعُونَتِهِ، وَأَفْضَلَ عَلَيْهِمْ مِنْ جِدَتِهِ بِمَا يَسَعُهُمْ يَسَعُ مَنْ وَرَاءَهُمْ مِنْ خُلُوفِ أَهْلِيهِمْ حَتَّى يَكُونَ هَمُّهُمْ هَمّاً وَاحِداً فِي جِهَادِ الْعَدُوِّ، فَإِنَّ عَطْفَكَ عَلَيْهِمْ يَعْطِفُ قُلُوبَهُمْ عَلَيْكَ. وَإِنَّ أَفْضَلَ قُرَّةِ عَيْنِ الْوُلاَةِ اسْتِقَامَةُ الْعَدْلِ فِي الْبِلاَدِ، وَظُهُورُ مَوَدَّةِ الرَّعِيَّةِ، وَإِنَّهُ لاَ تَظْهَرُ مَوَدَّتُهُمْ إِلاَّ بَسَلاَمَةِ صُدُورِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَصِحُّ نَصِيحَتُهُمْ إِلاّ بِحِيطَتِهِمْ عَلَى وُلاَةِ أُمُورِهِمْ، وَقِلَّةِ اسْتِثْقَالِ دُوَلِهِمْ، وَتَرْكِ اسْتِبْطَاءِ انْقِطَاعِ مُدَّتِهِمْ. فَافْسَحْ فِي آمَالِهِمْ، وَوَاصِلْ فِي حُسْنِ الثَّنَاءِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَتَعْدِيدِ مَا أَبْلى ذَوُالْبَلاَءِ مِنْهُمْ، فَإِنَّ كَثْرَةَ الذِّكْرِ لِحُسْنِ أَفْعَالِهِمْ تَهُزُّ الشُّجَاعَ، وَتُحَرِّضُ النَّاكِلَ، إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ⟫

Acknowledge each soldier's true measure of service; do not conflate one's achievement with another's, nor diminish anyone's reward below the level of his performance. Let not a man's high station lead you to magnify his small deeds, nor his lowly rank to minimize his great ones.

⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ اعْرِفْ لِكُلِّ امْرِىء مِنْهُمْ مَا أَبْلى، وَلاَ تَضُمَّنَّ بَلاَءَ امْرِىء إِلَى غَيْرِهِ، وَلاَ تُقَصِّرَنَّ بِهِ دُونَ غَايَةِ بَلاَئِهِ، وَلاَ يَدْعُوَنَّكَ شَرَفُ امْرِىء إِلَى أَنْ تُعْظِمَ مِنْ بَلاَئِهِ مَا كَانَ صَغِيراً، وَلاَضَعَةُ امْرِىء إِلَى أَنْ تَسْتَصْغِرَ مِنْ يَلاَئِهِ مَاكَانَ عَظيِماً⟫

When you are perplexed about a matter, refer it to Allah and His Prophet; for Allah has addressed the believers, saying:

> ⟪quran 4:59⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوٓا۟ أَطِيعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا۟ ٱلرَّسُولَ وَأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَمْرِ مِنكُمْ ۖ فَإِن تَنَزَعْتُمْ فِى شَىْءٍۢ فَرُدُّوهُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِ وَٱلرَّسُولِ إِن كُنتُمْ تُؤْمِنُونَ بِٱللَّهِ وَٱلْيَوْمِ ٱلْآخِرِ ۚ ذَلِكَ خَيْرٌۭ وَأَحْسَنُ تَأْوِيلًا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Obey Allah and obey the Messenger and those in authority among you. And if you dispute among yourselves about anything, refer it to Allah and His Messenger, if you believe in Allah and the Last Day. That is better and better in the end.*
> — **Quran 4:59**

<!-- section 11 (id=3594, raw_sort=11): Justice and Tyranny -->

## Justice and Tyranny

Justice (*ʿadl*) in the hereafter exists only when all things are established in their proper ranks and stations in both this world and the next. When we examine this principle in the governmental and social sphere, we discover that justice emerges as the fruit of piety (*taqwā*, godconsciousness) and righteousness. Ali teaches that as the ruler holds rights over his subjects, so do the subjects hold rights over him. A ruler cannot be righteous unless his subjects are righteous, and conversely, subjects cannot fulfill their obligations unless the ruler is just. When subjects honor the rights of their ruler and the ruler honors the rights of his subjects, truth is respected, the paths of religion prevail, and the banners of justice are raised.

This emphasis on the ruler's piety is not accidental. When we examine the life of Amīr al-Muʾminīn, we find his entire conduct grounded in these divine principles. Consider a single instance: upon assuming the caliphate after ʿUthmān's assassination, his cousin Ibn ʿAbbās advised him to retain the governors appointed by ʿUthmān provisionally until he had consolidated his government. Ali replied: "I have no doubt that your counsel reflects worldly wisdom. But I am bound by the *al-adhā yalzamuni min al-haqq*—an obligation to truth that supersedes political expediency. When I discern the truth about ʿUthmān's governors, how can I keep them in place?" He thus deposed Mu'āwiya and all other governors immediately. Though historians have regarded this as a political miscalculation—Mu'āwiya wanted only Syrian rule and might have accepted it—Ali viewed such compromise as surrender of religion for worldly advantage. As he himself stated: "When people abandon part of their religion for the sake of the world, Allah opens gates of further trials upon them in this world." Retaining known oppressors would have constituted exactly such a compromise, unimaginable to one whose hatred of this world's superfluities was absolute.[^cite-26]

In this letter to Malik al-Ashtar, addressed to one of his most trusted disciples, the warnings against oppression and tyranny carry particular weight. These instructions are not merely for the just-minded who naturally incline toward righteous rule, but for those who, though they intellectually embrace the philosophy of justice, possess the latent capacity to be seduced by power. For when the intoxication of authority rises, it can transform even a just ruler into a tyrant.

The potential for evil dwells in every human soul. When this potential combines with the instruments of power and the ruler is deprived of divine support and constant vigilance, that latent evil becomes actual. Therefore, at the letter's outset, Ali commands: "Give priority to the obedience of Allah over all else! Obey the ordinances in His Book, for whoever follows them attains felicity (*saʿāda*), and whoever denies them and neglects them attains wretchedness (*shaqāwa*)." This preamble is far more than mere notification; it is liberating. Obedience to Allah is not merely obligatory but grants spiritual freedom. This constraint frees the soul from the despotism of the base self (*nafs*), because the soul "commands toward evil save when Allah's mercy is upon it."[^cite-27]

⟪quran 12:53⟫
⟪ar:‏ وَمَآ أُبَرِّئُ نَفْسِىٓ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلنَّفْسَ لَأَمَّارَةٌۢ بِٱلسُّوٓءِ إِلَّا مَا رَحِمَ رَبِّىٓ ۚ إِنَّ رَبِّى غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
*"And I do not acquit myself. Verily, the soul incites to evil, except when my Lord bestows His mercy. Indeed, my Lord is Forgiving and Merciful."*

This verse illuminates the dialectic between divine mercy (*raḥma*) and the self. Without this mercy, the soul inclines toward sin and evil. But by Allah's grace, the soul escapes the snare of desires and appetites, returning to its primordial nature (*fiṭra*). The Qur'an speaks of this restored state:

> ⟪quran 89:27-29⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيَّتُهَا ٱلنَّفْسُ ٱلْمُطْمَئِنَّةُ ‎ ‏ٱرْجِعِىٓ إِلَىٰ رَبِّكِ رَاضِيَةًۭ مَّرْضِيَّةًۭ ‎ ‏فَٱدْخُلِى فِى عِبَدِى ‎⟫
> *"O soul at peace! Return unto your Lord, pleased and pleasing. Enter among My servants, and enter My paradise."*

The self thus stands at its origin and returns to its origin, for the soul is inscribed with divine nature and its homecoming is to that state of primordial harmony.

## Spirituality and Moral Character

In his first sermon (*khutba*), Amīr al-Muʾminīn proclaims:

⟪ar-quote:وَاصْطَفى سُبْحَانَهُ مِنْ وَلَدِهِ أَنْبيَاءَ أَخَذَ عَلَى الْوَحْيِ مِيثَاقَهُم، وَعَلَى تَبْليغِ الرِّسَالَةِ أَمَانَتَهُمْ، لَمَّا بَدَّلَ أَكْثَرُ خَلْقِهِ عَهْدَ اللهِ إِلَيْهِمْ، فَجَهِلُوا حَقَّهُ، واتَّخَذُوا الاْنْدَادَ مَعَهُ، وَاجْتَالَتْهُمُ الشَّيَاطِينُ عَنْ مَعْرفَتِهِ، وَاقتَطَعَتْهُمْ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ، فَبَعَثَ فِيهمْ رُسُلَهُ، وَوَاتَرَ إِلَيْهِمْ أَنْبِياءَهُ،**لِيَسْتَأْدُوهُمْ مِيثَاقَ فِطْرَتِهِ**، وَيُذَكِّرُوهُمْ مَنْسِيَّ نِعْمَتِهِ، وَيَحْتَجُّوا عَلَيْهِمْ بَالتَّبْلِيغِ، **وَيُثِيرُوا لَهُمْ دَفَائِنَ الْعُقُولِ**، وَيُرُوهُمْ آيَاتِ الْمَقْدِرَةِ⟫

"Allah selected from His creation prophets and pledged them with revelation and entrusted them with His message. When most of His creatures had perverted the covenant Allah made with them, forgetting His due and taking compeers with Him, when Satan turned them away from knowing Him and kept them from His worship, Allah sent His Messengers and sent them prophets in succession **

<!-- section 13 (id=3596, raw_sort=13): کبر اور غرور سے بچنے کی نصیحت -->

## Warning Against Arrogance and Self-Aggrandizement

The Imam admonishes the wrongdoer with a stark warning: "Do not prepare your soul for war with Allah!" This injunction points to a subtle but profound truth—that certain inward attitudes, though they may wear the garments of worldly action, constitute a spiritual enmity toward the Divine. When we examine such attitudes closely, we discover that their apparent evil lies not merely in the deed itself, but in the thinking that animates them, a thinking that runs counter to the very spirit those actions ought to embody.

Arrogance (kibr) furnishes an illuminating example. Maulana ʿAlī has warned against this vice repeatedly throughout his teachings. When a ruler becomes arrogant, he usurps one of the great attributes of Allah (Allāh). He claims for himself a dignity that belongs to Allah alone, for the title ⟪ar:'المتکبر'⟫ (al-Mutakabbir, the Mighty One) is worthy of the Divine Essence alone. To boast before people and display one's greatness is, in its hidden reality, to oppose Allah inwardly and to deny His ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫ (aḥadiyya, His Oneness). This concealed denial can be understood as waging war against Allah. The enmity toward ⟪ar:الحق⟫ (al-Ḥaqq, the Truth)—the hidden substance beneath a ruler's arrogance, pride, and oppression—reveals itself in every form of domination he exercises over those beneath him. When a ruler considers himself superior to his subjects, he simultaneously declares rebellion against his Lord above him. Thus the oppressor inflicts upon himself not only the Creator's just wrath through his cruelty to creatures, but also opposes the Creator through his very actions.[^cite-11] The root of this worldly evil is a spiritual defect arising from the denial of the Lord's ⟪ar:أحدیت⟫ (Oneness), His ⟪ar:حقانیت⟫ (ḥaqāniyya, His inherent Right), and from forgetfulness of the Qur'anic verse:

> ⟪quran 40:16⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَوْمَ هُم بَرِزُونَۖ لَا يَخْفَىٰ عَلَى ٱللَّهِ مِنْهُمْ شَىْءٌ ۭۚ لِّمَنِ ٱلْمُلْكُ ٱلْيَوْمَۖ لِلَّهِ ٱلْوَحِدِ ٱلْقَهَّارِ ‎⟫
> *The Day when they will (all) come out, nothing of them will be hidden from Allah. Whose is the kingdom this Day? (Allah Himself will reply to His Question): It is Allah's, the One, the Irresistible!*

This verse refers not only to the Last Day but to every day. In his celebrated sermon known as the ⟪ar:'القاصیۃ'⟫ (al-Qāṣiyya), the Imam describes the humiliation that befell the proud Iblīs, declaring him the first to confront Allah in the realm of arrogance—and thus the very source and center of all arrogance that would follow. When Allah commanded him to prostrate before Adam, Iblīs refused outright, filled with immense pride. He deemed himself superior to Adam, saying, "I am created of fire, and man is created of clay."[^cite-12] Because of this arrogance, Iblīs became not only the first enemy of Allah but also the leader of all the arrogant—⟪ar:أمام المتعصبین و صلف المستکبرین⟫ (imām al-mutaʿaṣṣibīn wa-ṣilf al-mustakbirīn)—who would come after him. The Imam therefore warns the ruler: "Beware of the sickness his whispers produce! Wear always the cloak of humility! Crush self-praise beneath your feet! Keep the fetters of arrogance from your neck! and fortify yourselves in the safe fortress of humility."

This teaching reveals that humility is the supreme weapon against Satan, for the Devil's true purpose is to sow arrogance in the human heart. Arrogance is not merely a grave vice in itself; it is a poison that corrupts every other virtue—⟪ar:خصال محمودۃ⟫ (khiṣāl maḥmūda)—that might otherwise adorn the soul. What is good becomes evil when pride attends it. As the Imam observes, "A sin that grieves you is better than a good deed that makes you arrogant." Times of praise and glory provide Satan his best opportunities for assault.[^cite-13]

*Verses referenced in this topic (curated linkage from KASHKOLE. TopicAyats — 7 of 7 not already cited above):*

> ⟪quran 7:181⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎⟫
> *And of those whom We have created, there is a community who guides (others) with the truth, and establishes justice therewith.*

> ⟪quran 7:182⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *Those who reject Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.), We shall gradually seize them with punishment in ways they perceive not.*

> ⟪quran 9:85⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تُعْجِبْكَ أَمْوَلُهُمْ وَأَوْلَدُهُمْ ۚ إِنَّمَا يُرِيدُ ٱللَّهُ أَن يُعَذِّبَهُم بِهَا فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَتَزْهَقَ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَهُمْ كَفِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *And let not their wealth or their children amaze you. Allah's Plan is to punish them with these things in this world, and that their souls shall depart (die) while they are disbelievers.*

> ⟪quran 17:81⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَقُلْ جَآءَ ٱلْحَقُّ وَزَهَقَ ٱلْبَطِلُ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلْبَطِلَ كَانَ زَهُوقًۭا ‎⟫
> *And say: "Truth (i.e. Islamic Monotheism or this Quran or Jihad against polytheists) has come and Batil (falsehood, i.e. Satan or polytheism, etc.) has vanished. Surely! Batil is ever bound to vanish." *

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*

> ⟪quran 55:26⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish.*

> ⟪quran 55:27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*

<!-- section 14 (id=3601, raw_sort=14): شرک خفی -->

## Hidden Idolatry (*Shirk al-Khafī*)

Although the outward meaning of shirk (idolatry, polytheism) is understood as the worship of physical idols, a deeper and more perilous form exists: the worship of idols hidden within the self—idols that manifest themselves as false intentions, corrupt attitudes, base inclinations, pride, ostentation, boasting, and self-deception. The Prophet (upon whom be peace) alluded to this hidden form when he said, "Idolatry is hidden in my community like the tracks of a black ant upon a black stone in a black night." The Imam echoes this: "Know that even the slightest bit of hypocrisy (riyāʾ) is idolatry." Why? Because to act for the praise of others rather than for the sake of Allah is to associate partners with Him. Whoever acts for other than Allah will be entrusted by Allah to those others—abandoned to the very objects of his false devotion.[^cite-14]

Iblīs's inward arrogance led to his outward disobedience, which in turn brought him the fate of humiliation. He disobeyed Allah precisely because of his pride—a sequence that reveals arrogance itself to be inherently disgraceful, a seed of destruction. Consider how Allah humiliated him! To be arrogant is in truth to be humiliated; to exalt oneself is in reality to debase oneself. This is why the Imam counseled Malik al-Ashtar: "Do not say, 'I have the authority, I command and I am obeyed.'" Such a notion creates chaos in the heart and ruins religion itself.[^cite-15] From these words, we understand a vital principle: for religion to appear correctly in the world, the inner intentions and concepts must themselves be correct. The Imam therefore advises that when power rises to the head, faith departs from the heart. For faith to endure in this world, it must emerge from the heart and manifest as humility—another expression of justice, of keeping all things in their proper place.

The Imam then instructs Malik al-Ashtar further: "If your position makes you arrogant and proud, then look at the greatness of Allah, over whom you stand." This contemplation will help you overcome your desires and restore your intellect by protecting you from the rigidity of the self. The relationship between intellect and humility deserves reflection here. The intellect that grows distracted by arrogance and pretense loses the capacity to understand the reality of Allah and the truths that emanate from that reality. In Arabic, arrogance is called ⟪ar:'مَخِلا'⟫ (mikhāl), a term connected etymologically to *khiyāl* (imagination, illusion). Thus kibr itself is an "imagining," a deception rooted in this real yet deceptive world. Arrogance is a severe form of doubt that springs from a disordered intellect—it is reckoned evil, recognized as immoral. It concerns itself not only with inflating one's own estimation but ⟪ar:الحق⟫ (with belittling Truth).[^cite-16] Only one whom Allah has befriended—⟪ar:ولی اللہ⟫ (walī Allāh)—can grasp the reality contained in the following verses and draw from them that humility which erases ⟪ar:'أنائیت'⟫ (anāʾiyya, egoism) from its very root—the root of all arrogance, display, and pride, and the sustenance of every oppression:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*

> ⟪quran 55:26-27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎ ‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish. And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*

> ⟪quran 17:81⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَقُلْ جَآءَ ٱلْحَقُّ وَزَهَقَ ٱلْبَطِلُ ۚ إِنَّ ٱلْبَطِلَ كَانَ زَهُوقًۭا ‎⟫
> *And say: "Truth (i.e. Islamic Monotheism or this Quran or Jihad against polytheists) has come and Batil (falsehood, i.e. Satan or polytheism, etc.) has vanished. Surely! Batil is ever bound to vanish." *

With this understanding, the Imam's exhortation takes on fuller weight: "Be afraid of imitating Allah and contending with Him, for Allah despises every wrongdoer and humiliates every arrogant one." Whoever does not do justice to Allah and His creation will find that on the Day of Resurrection not only Allah's creation but Allah Himself stands against him. Man lives in a state of war with Allah until he abandons his oppression and returns in repentance. Even if he survives in this world, he will find no deliverance in the Hereafter.

The longer the oppressor persists in wrongdoing, the more his soul becomes diseased; the more it is soaked in suffering. The Qur'an presents this through the concept of ⟪ar:'استدراج'⟫ (istidraj, gradual seduction into ruin)—degrees of punishment that not only describe these stages but also clarify the distinction between those who establish justice with the truth and those who do wrong:

> ⟪quran 7:181-182⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَمِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَآ أُمَّةٌۭ يَهْدُونَ بِٱلْحَقِّ وَبِهِۦ يَعْدِلُونَ ‎ ‏وَٱلَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا۟ بِـَٔايَتِنَا سَنَسْتَدْرِجُهُم مِّنْ حَيْثُ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> *And of those whom We have created, there is a community who guides (others) with the truth, and establishes justice therewith. Those who reject Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.), We shall gradually seize them with punishment in ways they perceive not.*

Such punishment comes not only as poverty, illness, and suffering, but also—paradoxically—as worldly success, glory, and offspring, as Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 9:85⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تُعْجِبْكَ أَمْوَلُهُمْ وَأَوْلَدُهُمْ ۚ إِنَّمَا يُرِيدُ ٱللَّهُ أَن يُعَذِّبَهُم بِهَا فِى ٱلدُّنْيَا وَتَزْهَقَ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَهُمْ كَفِرُونَ ‎⟫
> *And let not their wealth or their children amaze you. Allah's Plan is to punish them with these things in this world, and that their souls shall depart (die) while they are disbelievers.*

The wrongdoer is ⟪ar:'مسلمان'⟫ (a Muslim in appearance) and yet simultaneously ⟪ar:'کافر'⟫ (a concealer of truth, a denier) by virtue of his kufr (the hiding of what is true). He has veiled the truth from himself through his deeds, covering it with everything of good that might otherwise flow from it.

<!-- section 15 (id=3597, raw_sort=15): اخلاقی و روحانی ضمیر -->

## The Moral and Spiritual Conscience

Another form of waging war against Allah is to fight one's "voice of conscience"—that inner voice which, arising from a soul that knows and understands its moral obligations, speaks to the self as the awakened witness of the heart. The voice of conscience is, in truth, the voice of an awakened soul.

> ⟪quran 91:7-8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَنَفْسٍۢ وَمَا سَوَّىٰهَا ‎ ‏فَأَلْهَمَهَا فُجُورَهَا وَتَقْوَىٰهَا ‎⟫
> *And by Nafs (Adam or a person or a soul, etc.), and Him Who perfected him in proportion; Then He showed him what is wrong for him and what is right for him;*

This verse teaches us that the soul, when it is perfected, becomes a guide toward the right path. It is the conscience—⟪ar:نفس⟫⟪ar:أمارۃ بالسوء⟫ (al-nafs al-ʾammāra bi-l-suʾ, the commanding soul)—upon which good and evil arguments both bear witness. A morally awakened soul will inspire virtue; a low and degraded soul will inspire wickedness. Allah has placed within every soul, amid its conscience, a capacity for discernment—to which the above verse alludes. Therefore every soul not only distinguishes between good and evil but also instinctively recognizes both its own ⟪ar:'عبدیت'⟫ (ʿubūdiyya, servanthood) and Allah's ⟪ar:'الہیت'⟫ (ilāhiyya, Divinity). The Qur'an recounts the moment when Allah created humanity and drew from them a covenant acknowledging His Lordship:

> ⟪quran 7:172⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنۢ بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ۖ قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ ۛ أَن تَقُولُوا۟ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And (remember) when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam, from their loins, their seed (or from Adam's loin his offspring) and made them testify as to themselves (saying): "Am I not your Lord?" They said: "Yes! We testify," lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection: "Verily, we have been unaware of this." *

This reveals that the wrongdoer is one who breaks this primordial covenant with Allah, taking himself—⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫ (the commanding, base self)—as lord in place of true faith in Allah. For this reason, ʿAlī counseled Malik al-Ashtar: "Do not say, 'I command, and obey me,'" for such is the way of that commanding self whose orders the body, soul, imagination, intellect, intention, emotions, and consciousness all obey.[^cite-17] The way to do justice to oneself is through ⟪ar:مجاہدۃ النفس⟫ (mujāhadat al-nafs, the struggle against the self)—to first remove one's own shortcomings. Thus the Imam said, "If you wish to reform others, you must first reform yourself, for trying to improve the souls of others while evil remains in yourself is the gravest of sins."

Before Malik al-Ashtar, the Imam had appointed ⟪ar:محمد بن ابی بکر⟫ (Muḥammad ibn Abī Bakr) as the governor of Egypt. To him too he gave counsel: "I have appointed you guardian of the people of Egypt. It is incumbent upon you by nature to contend against your own self and to protect your religion!" This statement of yours carries profound meaning. The Imam conferred upon Muḥammad two obligations: first, to master his own self and its desires; second, to safeguard his religion.[^cite-18] The greater the power and authority one possesses, the greater becomes one's responsibility to control the self and restrain its impulses. For if the soul becomes enslaved to desire and the ruler uses his authority to fulfill those desires, he destroys not only himself but religion itself. The outward expression of a Muslim's faith depends upon the inner integrity of the soul for its very survival. This too is an expression of keeping all things in their rightful place. When power ascends to the head, the Qur'an describes ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ⟫ (that base self which creates arrogance, the hunger for dominance and authority) in these terms:

> ⟪quran 96:6-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كَلَّآ إِنَّ ٱلْإِنسَنَ لَيَطْغَىٰٓ ‎ ‏أَن رَّآهُ ٱسْتَغْنَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *Nay! Verily, man does transgress all bounds (in disbelief and evil deed, etc.). Because he considers himself self-sufficient.*

The more a soul deceives itself with the illusion of autonomy and flees from trust in Allah, the more it will come to imagine itself as divine—the greatest injustice to itself. Such a soul becomes the one of whom Allah says:

> ⟪quran 45:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَرَءَيْتَ مَنِ ٱتَّخَذَ إِلَهَهُۥ هَوَىٰهُ وَأَضَلَّهُ ٱللَّهُ عَلَىٰ عِلْمٍۢ وَخَتَمَ عَلَىٰ سَمْعِهِۦ وَقَلْبِهِۦ وَجَعَلَ عَلَىٰ بَصَرِهِۦ غِشَوَةًۭ فَمَن يَهْدِيهِ مِنۢ بَعْدِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أَفَلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ ‎⟫
> *Have you seen him who takes his own lust (vain desires) as his ilah (god), and Allah knowing (him as such), left him astray, and sealed his hearing and his heart, and put a cover on his sight. Who then will guide him after Allah? Will you not then remember?*

The more a person acquires knowledge of his "worthlessness" and understands his need of Allah, the more ⟪ar:نفس امارۃ بالسوء⟫ (the grip of the commanding self) loosens from about his neck. This is so because only the soul that commands itself to evil can command others to evil; conversely, the soul that humbles itself before Allah treats people with humility, compassion, and justice.

The Imam says: "In my view, your deeds should be the most cherished in your eyes, the most just, the most righteous—precisely because the people's disapproval weakens when faced with the people's approval." You have insisted upon the approval of ordinary human beings in your words! The one who holds himself cheap in the sight of Allah will dwell at ease with common folk; the arrogant will seek only the company of the arrogant and will grasp correctly the verse:

> ⟪quran 35:15⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ أَنتُمُ ٱلْفُقَرَآءُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِۖ وَٱللَّهُ هُوَ ٱلْغَنِىُّ ٱلْحَمِيدُ ‎⟫
> *O mankind! it is you who stand in need of Allah, but Allah is Rich (Free of all wants and needs), Worthy of all praise.*

The life of Amīr al-Muʾminīn—the Master of the Believers—stands as testimony to these principles. Once, a member of the family of a ascetic complained to him that he was living in unnecessary poverty. The Imam called them and advised them to care for their families and not to spurn the gifts Allah had given. They replied, "O ʿAlī! You speak thus, yet you yourself are clothed only in a coarse garment and eat dry bread." The Imam responded, "Woe to you! I am not like you. Allah has made it obligatory upon the ⟪ar:ائمۃ الحق⟫ (aʾimmat al-Ḥaqq, the Guides of Truth) to live as the poorest of their people, so that they may feel the poverty of the poor and not fall prey to greed."[^cite-19] This incident teaches that a ruler must live his worldly life at the level of the poorest of his subjects. The Imam chose for himself the least that he could obtain. This was because he possessed a profound connection with ⟪ar:'الحق'⟫ (the Truth), by the light of which every material thing in the world became contemptible, despicable, and worthless in his sight.

<!-- section 16 (id=3587, raw_sort=16): عدل اور ہمدردی -->

## Justice and Compassion

The suffering of the poor awakens in a person a vivid sense of his dependence upon his Lord, allowing him to traverse life between hope and fear, cast upon Allah's mercy. Living in such awareness, the Fitrah—the natural disposition—moves him to treat his fellows with compassion and tender feeling. The capacity for empathy does not contradict the demands of justice; rather, it forms an essential component of justice itself. It not only assists in keeping all things in their rightful place but also accords with the nature of the universe and represents a supreme attribute of Truth. For this reason, Allah begins every chapter of the Qur'an with Bismillāh—ar-Raḥmān ar-Raḥīm (In the name of Allah, the Merciful, the Compassionate), in which He mentions His mercy and care. We observe this same behavior in the lives of the Prophet (upon whom be peace) and Amīr al-Muʾminīn—they always treated Allah's servants with mercy. Yet they did not do so from mere personal sentiment; rather, it was a duty owed to Allah, as He declared:

> ⟪quran 7:156⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ وَٱكْتُبْ لَنَا فِى هَذِهِ ٱلدُّنْيَا حَسَنَةًۭ وَفِى ٱلْآخِرَةِ إِنَّا هُدْنَآ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ عَذَابِىٓ أُصِيبُ بِهِۦ مَنْ أَشَآءُ ۖ وَرَحْمَتِى وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَىْءٍۢ ۚ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَٱلَّذِينَ هُم بِـَٔايَتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ ‎⟫
> *And ordain for us good in this world, and in the Hereafter. Certainly we have turned unto You." He said: (As to) My Punishment I afflict therewith whom I will and My Mercy embraces all things. That (Mercy) I shall ordain for those who are the Muttaqun (pious - see V.2:2), and give Zakat; and those who believe in Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs and revelations, etc.);*

> ⟪quran 6:54⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذَا جَآءَكَ ٱلَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِـَٔايَتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلَمٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ۖ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِ ٱلرَّحْمَةَ ۖ أَنَّهُۥ مَنْ عَمِلَ مِنكُمْ سُوٓءًۢا بِجَهَلَةٍۢ ثُمَّ تَابَ مِنۢ بَعْدِهِۦ وَأَصْلَحَ فَأَنَّهُۥ غَفُورٌۭ رَّحِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *When those who believe in Our Ayat (proofs, evidences, verses, lessons, signs, revelations, etc.) come to you, say: "Salamun 'Alaikum" (peace be on you); your Lord has written Mercy for Himself, so that, if any of you does evil in ignorance, and thereafter repents and does righteous good deeds (by obeying Allah), then surely, He is Oft­Forgiving, Most Merciful.*

In similar vein, the teachings of Maulana ʿAlī abound with exhortations to mercy. He said: "The act of showing mercy brings down Allah's mercy upon you; you will be shown mercy to the extent that you show mercy to others. And I marvel at one who hopes for mercy from above yet shows none to those below him."[^cite-20]

According to this principle, the more a person embodies compassion in his spiritual thoughts and moral character toward others, the nearer he draws to the Almighty. In a just society, people should be treated with compassion wherever it is possible to do so. Naturally, when no other recourse remains, severe punishments must be imposed. Thus in his letter to Malik al-Ashtar, the Imam instructed him to punish officers found guilty of usurping wealth so that Allah's justice might be established. Elsewhere, writing to a cousin whom he had appointed governor of Baṣra, he declared: "By Allah, I swear with utmost sincerity: if word reaches me that you have usurped Muslim wealth—whether little or great—I shall inflict upon you a punishment that will diminish your substance, break your back, and bring your deeds to ruin!"[^cite-21]

Whenever someone asked the Imam for a favor, he treated them with stern impartiality, even his own relatives. Once his brother ʿAqīl requested additional funds from the treasury. The Imam placed a burning piece of metal in his hand. As ʿAqīl cried out in pain, the Imam said, "Brother ʿAqīl, if you cannot bear this small fire, how shall I bear the blazing fire of Allah's Hell on the Day of Resurrection—the fire to which you invite me?"[^cite-22] Similarly, when he learned that his cousin ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAbbās had misappropriated Muslim wealth, he said to him: "Fear Allah and return to the people what belongs to them. If you do not, and Allah grants me power over you, I shall strike you with my sword, and whoever I strike has entered the realm of the jinn. By Allah, if even Ḥasan and Ḥusayn were to do the same, they would receive no concession from me."[^cite-23]

This demonstrates that regardless of status, everyone stands equal before the demands of justice. The Imam's conduct differed markedly from his predecessors, who distributed government among their relatives and plundered Muslim wealth. As he observed, "In springtime a camel swallows the tender shoots."[^cite-24] The Qur'an itself declares:

> ⟪quran 4:135⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ كُونُوا۟ قَوَّمِينَ بِٱلْقِسْطِ شُهَدَآءَ لِلَّهِ وَلَوْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِكُمْ أَوِ ٱلْوَلِدَيْنِ وَٱلْأَقْرَبِينَ ۚ إِن يَكُنْ غَنِيًّا أَوْ فَقِيرًۭا فَٱللَّهُ أَوْلَىٰ بِهِمَا ۖ فَلَا تَتَّبِعُوا۟ ٱلْهَوَىٰٓ أَن تَعْدِلُوا۟ ۚ وَإِن تَلْوُۥٓا۟ أَوْ تُعْرِضُوا۟ فَإِنَّ ٱللَّهَ كَانَ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ خَبِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Stand out firmly for justice, as witnesses to Allah, even though it be against yourselves, or your parents, or your kin, be he rich or poor, Allah is a Better Protector to both (than you). So follow not the lusts (of your hearts), lest you may avoid justice, and if you distort your witness or refuse to give it, verily, Allah is Ever Well­Acquainted with what you do.*

The following passage from the Imam's letter merits particular attention, for in it he places compassion within a universal context, establishing all humankind on a level of equality. In this statement lies a cure for all forms of prejudice and sectarianism:

⟪ar-quote:وَأَشْعِرْ قَلْبَكَ الرَّحْمَةَ لِلرَّعِيَّةِ، وَالْـمَحَبَّةَ لَهُمْ، وَاللُّطْفَ بِهِمْ، وَلاَ تَكُونَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ سَبُعاً ضَارِياً تَغْتَنِمُ أَكْلَهُمْ، فَإِنَّهُمْ صِنْفَانِ- إِمَّا أَخٌ لَكَ فِي الدِّينِ، وَإمّا نَظِيرٌ لَكَ فِي الْخَلْقِ، يَفْرُطُ مِنْهُمُ الزَّلَلُ، وَتَعْرِضُ لَهُمُ الْعِلَلُ،يُؤْتَى عَلَى أَيْدِيهِمْ فِي الَعَمْدِ وَالْخَطَاَ، فَأَعْطِهِمْ مِنْ عَفْوِكَ وَصَفْحِكَ مِثْلَ الَّذِي تُحِبُّ أَنْ يُعْطِيَكَ اللهُ مِنْ عَفْوِهِ وَصَفْحِهِ، فَإِنَّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ، وَ وَالِي الاْمْرِ عَلَيْكَ فَوْقَكَ، وَاللهُ فَوْقَ مَنْ وَلاَّكَ! وَقَدِ اسْتَكْفَاكَ أَمْرَهُمْ، وَابْتَلاَكَ بِهِمْ⟫

Habituate your heart to mercy for the subjects and to affection and kindness for them. Do not stand over them like greedy beasts who feel it is enough to devour them, since they are of two kinds: either your brother in religion or one like you in creation. They will commit slips and encounter mistakes. They may act wrongly, whether wilfully or through neglect. So, extend to them your forgiveness and pardon, in the same way as you would like Allah to extend His forgiveness and pardon to you, because you are over them and your responsible Commander (the Imam) is over you while Allah is over him who has appointed you. He (Allah) has sought you to manage their affairs and has tried you through them.[^cite-25]

By admonishing mercy for all humankind, you have drawn attention to Allah's mercy itself. Every person, no matter how great a ruler or king, remains a servant of Allah and exists in complete need of His mercy. When a person recognizes that he holds authority over another human being, he should remember that he himself stands in submission before Allah. This awareness will make him kind and sympathetic to those beneath him and will draw Allah's mercy toward him. He reminded Malik al-Ashtar that although he is a ruler, he is a human being like all others.

Once Maulana ʿAlī observed a blind mendicant who was seeking alms but no one was giving to him. When told that he was Christian, the Imam replied, "You have taken so much from him that he has grown old and weak, and now you refuse to help him. From today, let him be supported from the state treasury."[^cite-26] This action teaches that both Muslims and non-Muslims stand equal before the demands of justice. Social justice and compassionate treatment arise from mercy; therefore, mercy is a binding duty upon all Muslims.

The Imam told Malik al-Ashtar that his rule was not a gift from Allah but a test and trial—a truth he had demonstrated throughout his own caliphate. In one of his sermons he declared: "Had not Allah promised the learned ones that they would stand against the oppressor and support the oppressed, I would have cast the reins of this caliphate upon his neck, and you would have seen that this world is to me more worthless than the substance that flows from a goat's nostrils."[^cite-27] Here we find an echo of Plato's teaching that the true philosopher is one who rules only for the sake of the people—not considering it an honor for himself but an inescapable duty, with the sole aim of establishing justice. For the establishment and restoration of any society rests upon this single attribute alone.

From the Imam's teachings we learn that government and power operate under the principle of welfare for the poor. When Allah bestows upon one of His servants the blessing of knowledge and grants him the consciousness of justice, his responsibility increases proportionally. The greater the divine grace upon a person, the greater becomes his obligation to show favor to Allah's creatures. In one of his sermons, he declared: "Allah's grace does not increase toward a servant unless Allah's right becomes great in his eyes."[^cite-28]

<!-- section 17 (id=3588, raw_sort=17): اللہ کے بارے میں خوش گمانی -->

## Good Assumption Toward Allah (*Husnā al-Zann bi-Allāh*)

Let us now turn to that portion of Amīr al-Muʾminīn's letter in which he advised Malik al-Ashtar regarding the choice of ministers and counselors. He instructed him to avoid the miserly and the cowardly, saying: "Truly, stinginess, cowardice, and greed arise from a deficiency of trust in Allah." Such mistrust springs from a failure to understand the Divine Fitrah—the natural disposition—and ignorance of Fitrah itself arises from inadequate knowledge of Allah's attributes. From this perspective, all human vice is connected to a deterioration of intellect caused by weakness of faith. Conversely, a strong faith produces right estimation of Allah, a vigorous intellect, and a sound conception of the Divine Reality, which illuminates within it the divine attributes themselves. One should not suppose that because these attributes belong to Allah, one ought to refrain from acquiring them. Rather, a person should take these qualities as examples for himself and as the manner of his life, removing the defects of the soul. This does not mean that a person competes with the greatness of Allah, but rather that the aim is to become similar to Allah.[^cite-29] This spiritual development is achieved through the worship of Allah. In other words, a person should be generous because Allah is generous, and merciful because Allah is merciful. Yet at the same time, he must establish within himself humility and devotion, understanding that he can never develop within himself any quality that matches the attributes of Allah!

All of Allah's attributes describe man's absolute dependence upon and need of Allah, as well as His Unity and Uniqueness. In this way, both a positive and a negative relationship is established between Allah and His servant. The positive aspect appears in the Imam's saying that whoever does not show mercy to another, Allah does not show mercy to him. The negative aspect appears in Allah's declaration:

> ⟪quran 35:15⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ أَنتُمُ ٱلْفُقَرَآءُ إِلَى ٱللَّهِۖ وَٱللَّهُ هُوَ ٱلْغَنِىُّ ٱلْحَمِيدُ ‎⟫
> *O mankind! it is you who stand in need of Allah, but Allah is Rich (Free of all wants and needs), Worthy of all praise.*

In this synthesis lies the truth that human virtue and moral excellence are reflections of Allah's divine attributes, while the conviction that one exists in a state of non-being before Allah's majesty maintains the correct relationship. A person is simultaneously the representative of Allah and His servant—⟪ar:خلیفۃ اللہ و عبد اللہ⟫ (khalīfat Allāh wa-ʿabd Allāh). His servitude keeps him within the bounds of servanthood lest he transgress and become a partner in Allah's glory; his representation reminds him that consciousness of his servitude to Allah must not make him forget his obligation toward Allah's creation, which Allah has enjoined upon him. This balance between representation and servitude, between duty to Allah and duty to His servants, is yet another expression of keeping all things in their proper place—a means of establishing harmony between moral practice and spiritual purification.

<!-- section 18 (id=3590, raw_sort=18): شہر اور معاشرا -->

## City and Society

The Imam then addresses in his letter the various segments of society—the military, the administrative officials, judges, governors, tax collectors, cultivators, merchants, craftsmen, and the destitute—and describes their respective duties. The counsel he offers regarding them may be seen as justice rendered practical. The ruler must fulfill the rights of all these classes while recognizing their duty to Allah. This is because Allah has established all these classes, has assigned them their sustenance and station, has set boundaries for each, and has taken from them a pledge to abide by the Qur'an and Sunnah.

The ruler's obligation to society forms part of his covenant with Allah, as he declared:

> ⟪quran 13:19-20⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ أَفَمَن يَعْلَمُ أَنَّمَآ أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِن رَّبِّكَ ٱلْحَقُّ كَمَنْ هُوَ أَعْمَىٰٓ ۚ إِنَّمَا يَتَذَكَّرُ أُو۟لُوا۟ ٱلْأَلْبَبِ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ يُوفُونَ بِعَهْدِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَا يَنقُضُونَ ٱلْمِيثَقَ ‎⟫
> *Shall he then who knows that what has been revealed unto you (O Muhammad PBUH) from your Lord is the truth be like him who is blind? But it is only the men of understanding that pay heed. Those who fulfill the Covenant of Allah and break not the Mîthaq (bond, treaty, covenant);*

And he said:

> ⟪quran 17:34⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَقْرَبُوا۟ مَالَ ٱلْيَتِيمِ إِلَّا بِٱلَّتِى هِىَ أَحْسَنُ حَتَّىٰ يَبْلُغَ أَشُدَّهُۥ ۚ وَأَوْفُوا۟ بِٱلْعَهْدِ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلْعَهْدَ كَانَ مَسْـُٔولًۭا ‎⟫
> *And come not near to the orphan's property except to improve it, until he attains the age of full strength. And fulfil (every) covenant. Verily! the covenant, will be questioned about.*

The Imam then advises the ruler to keep the company of scholars and wise men so that they may bring prosperity to his government and increase in his lands the welfare that his predecessors enjoyed. He then mentions each class separately, designating the ruler as the center around which all society revolves. The center, he explains, is nothing but the circle that connects it and the whole of society to Allah.

He first addresses the military, describing them as a fortress for the people. For the selection of the military commander, he says: "Choose one who is most sincere to Allah, His Messenger, and the Imam of the Age—whose heart is pure and clear, who is forbearing, slow to anger, quick to forgive, gentle with the weak, and stern with the strong; one who does not panic in difficulty and cannot be stopped by weakness." If we contemplate these qualities, we see them all prominently displayed in the character of the Prophet (upon whom be peace). The emphasis the Imam places upon compassion, gentleness, and forbearance is noteworthy, for these are not qualities ordinarily associated with warfare, since warriors are fond of fighting and death. Yet what is required is a brave warrior—fierce only toward enemies but also toward his own people—as the Qur'an states:

> ⟪quran 48:29⟫
> ⟪ar:‏مُّحَمَّدٌۭ رَّسُولُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ وَٱلَّذِينَ مَعَهُۥٓ أَشِدَّآءُ عَلَى ٱلْكُفَّارِ رُحَمَآءُ بَيْنَهُمْ ۖ تَرَىٰهُمْ رُكَّعًۭا سُجَّدًۭا يَبْتَغُونَ فَضْلًۭا مِّنَ ٱللَّهِ وَرِضْوَنًۭا ۖ سِيمَاهُمْ فِى وُجُوهِهِم مِّنْ أَثَرِ ٱلسُّجُودِ ۚ ذَلِكَ مَثَلُهُمْ فِى ٱلتَّوْرَىٰةِ ۚ وَمَثَلُهُمْ فِى ٱلْإِنجِيلِ كَزَرْعٍ أَخْرَجَ شَطْـَٔهُۥ فَـَٔازَرَهُۥ فَٱسْتَغْلَظَ فَٱسْتَوَىٰ عَلَىٰ سُوقِهِۦ يُعْجِبُ ٱلزُّرَّاعَ لِيَغِيظَ بِهِمُ ٱلْكُفَّارَ ۗ وَعَدَ ٱللَّهُ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ مِنْهُم مَّغْفِرَةًۭ وَأَجْرًا عَظِيمًۢا ‎⟫
> *Muhammad (PBUH) is the Messenger of Allah, and those who are with him are severe against disbelievers, and merciful among themselves. You see them bowing and falling down prostrate (in prayer), seeking Bounty from Allah and (His) Good Pleasure. The mark of them (i.e. of their Faith) is on their faces (foreheads) from the traces of (their) prostration (during prayers). This is their description in the Taurat (Torah). But their description in the Injeel (Gospel) is like a (sown) seed which sends forth its shoot, then makes it strong, it then becomes thick, and it stands straight on its stem, delighting the sowers that He may enrage the disbelievers with them. Allah has promised those among them who believe (i.e. all those who follow Islamic Monotheism, the religion of Prophet Muhammad PBUH till the Day of Resurrection) and do righteous good deeds, forgiveness and a mighty reward (i.e. Paradise).*

Regarding the judges, he specifies that they should be persons not confused by complex matters, not irritated by constant petitions, as firm as mountains in matters of truth, not satisfied with superficial tactics, skilled in debate, seekers of truth, and protected from praise and desire. He remarks that such people are indeed rare. He further advises that judges be compensated generously so that they do not become dependent upon the wealthy for sustenance.

With respect to the wise counselors, he says their integrity must be tested before they assume office, and there should be no favor or bias in their selection. Even after their appointment, their conduct should be scrutinized, and severe punishment should follow any abuse of their trust.

Concerning the peasants who cultivate the land and from whom revenue is collected, he advises: "Be more concerned with cultivating the land than with collecting revenue, for if the land is not cultivated, there will be no revenue. Whoever establishes a tax without inspecting the cultivation destroys the people."[^cite-30] He states that the ruin of the earth comes from the ruin of those who dwell upon it. Poverty befalls them when the desire to accumulate wealth dominates the hearts of the wise, when they doubt their own survival, and when they cannot benefit from the best examples. To doubt one's survival means to think oneself immortal and exempt from accountability. Allah addresses such people:

> ⟪quran 104:1-4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيْلٌۭ لِّكُلِّ هُمَزَةٍۢ لُّمَزَةٍ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِى جَمَعَ مَالًۭا وَعَدَّدَهُۥ ‎ ‏يَحْسَبُ أَنَّ مَالَهُۥٓ أَخْلَدَهُۥ ‎ ‏كَلَّا ۖ لَيُنۢبَذَنَّ فِى ٱلْحُطَمَةِ ‎⟫
> *Woe to every slanderer and backbiter. Who has gathered wealth and counted it, He thinks that his wealth will make him last forever! Nay! Verily, he will be thrown into the crushing Fire.*

When a person forgets that nothing endures, he develops an insatiable hunger to accumulate. Instead of acquiring true spiritual treasures, he spends his life gathering false material wealth, and as a consequence, oppression is born.[^cite-31]

Regarding the selection of state officials, the Imam teaches that one should not judge people merely by the qualities they now display, but should examine their past conduct and the public estimation of them, granting office only to those of established trustworthiness.

Concerning merchants, he says they benefit society greatly and should therefore be treated with utmost care. These are generally peace-loving people and should be free to conduct their business, yet the evils that arise among them—hoarding, miserliness, and deception—must be prevented.

### The Poor, Who Need Justice Most

About the poor, the disabled, the orphans, and the elderly, Amīr al-Muʾminīn declares that these are the people most in need of the ruler's justice, yet they are those least able to pursue their grievances. He said: "The ruler should take special care of these people if he wishes Allah to forgive him on the Day of Resurrection."[^cite-32] He should appoint a special officer to attend to their needs and bring their concerns before him. Then he continues: "This is a burden for the ruler, but Allah makes it easy for those who set their hopes on the Hereafter, who exhort themselves to patience, and who are certain in Allah's promise."

Here once again the Imam links the difficulty of this task to spiritual reality—that if one looks beyond this world toward the Hereafter, even the most arduous duty becomes manageable. But those whose desire remains fixed upon the world fall victim to negligence toward the poor. From a worldly perspective, aiding the poor brings no political advantage to the ruler, for the expenditure of state welfare for them yields no apparent benefit. Yet when this outlook is accompanied by consciousness of Allah's almighty justice, His abundant mercy, and the desire to earn the Hereafter through service to these people, the task becomes light, and the rulers of that time are moved to sincere support of them.

This approach transcends mere generosity and charity. When a person elevates the concept of aid to the poor to its highest perfection, he will not become a victim of selfish desire, selfishness, or unintentional negligence. Upon developing this quality, the next virtue described by Maulana ʿAlī—patience—arises spontaneously, for this act is not confined to personal effort and will but accompanied by divine grace flowing from the roots of faith. As a result, such people believe in God's reward, His justice, and His promise of mercy, and the ruler's determination to help the poor and establish justice becomes unshakeable.

These moral truths regarding the reality of the Hereafter remain hidden from the eyes of worldly rulers, obscured by their hidden prejudices and outward evil. Such wrongdoers do not believe in the blessings of the Hereafter, nor in its punishments and trials. They were called oppressors because they disobeyed the requirements of divine justice and denied that supreme attribute of mercy which is the very essence of God's nature.[^cite-33]


<!-- section 19 (id=3591, raw_sort=19): نیت کی اہمیت -->

## The Importance of Intention

The most important element among all the commands you have issued is *niyyah* (intention). Even if a person's efforts to establish justice cannot reach full fruition owing to the impermanence of this world, a sincere intention becomes the foundation of moral life and fills the soul with a taste of Allah's grace. If God's promise is true, and if man believes in this truth, then such belief possesses a transformative power over the soul: it converts a personal aspiration into an unconditional necessity, and a desirable attribute into an irrefutable reality. This reveals that morality is fortified by spirituality, and only then do all the Sharīʿah (Islamic law) commandments become light. Thereafter, a person establishes justice in gratitude for what he has already received from Allah, not in hope of what he shall receive in the Hereafter. The Qur'an speaks of Paradise's blessings as if they had already been bestowed upon the believers, as though what is yet to come has already transpired:[^cite-18]

> ⟪quran 108:1-2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّآ أَعْطَيْنَكَ ٱلْكَوْثَرَ ‎ ‏فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَٱنْحَرْ ‎⟫
> *Verily, We have granted you (O Muhammad (Peace be upon him)) Al-Kauthar (a river in Paradise); Therefore turn in prayer to your Lord and sacrifice (to Him only).*
> Indeed We have given you abundance, so perform the prayer to your Lord and sacrifice.
> — **Quran 108:1-2**

In explanation of this principle, Mawlānā ʿAlī distinguishes three orders of worship. There is a group that worships Allah out of desire for Paradise—this is commercial worship. Another group worships from fear of Hell—this is the worship of the slave. And there is a group that worships Allah out of gratitude—this is the worship of the free.[^cite-19] For this reason he declared in one place: ⟪ar-quote:یا الہی ما عبدتک من شوق جنتک ولا من خوف النارك بل وجدت مستحق لی العبادۃ فالعبدتک⟫ "O Allah, I do not worship You in the longing for Paradise, nor in fear of Your fire; rather I have found You worthy of worship, and so I worship You."

A person is absolved of the deficiencies in his deeds through the sincerity of his *niyyah*, for his action does not depend upon outcome but upon the purity of intention. Justice is not established for any worldly end, but to fulfill the intrinsic requirements of justice itself, since the justice of the just person is part of his essential nature. Justice is not ascribed to Allah in the sense that He performs justice; rather, He *is* just, and thus justice flows from His being. For this reason, the just person acts justly in order to align with the divine will, not merely to obey a command, nor from worldly ambition. Allah says:

> ⟪quran 92:17-21⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَسَيُجَنَّبُهَا ٱلْأَتْقَى ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِى يُؤْتِى مَالَهُۥ يَتَزَكَّىٰ ‎ ‏وَمَا لِأَحَدٍ عِندَهُۥ مِن نِّعْمَةٍۢ تُجْزَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِلَّا ٱبْتِغَآءَ وَجْهِ رَبِّهِ ٱلْأَعْلَىٰ ‎ ‏وَلَسَوْفَ يَرْضَىٰ ‎⟫
> *And Al-Muttaqun (the pious and righteous - see V.2:2) will be far removed from it (Hell). He who spends his wealth for increase in self-purification, And have in his mind no favour from anyone for which a reward is expected in return, Except only the desire to seek the Countenance of his Lord, the Most High; He surely will be pleased (when he will enter Paradise).*
> And away from it is the God-fearing one who gives his wealth so that he may be purified; and no soul has any favour against it, but he who is recompensed only with the Countenance of his Lord, the Most High, and he shall soon be well-pleased.
> — **Quran 92:17-21**

This is the definition of *al-abrār* (the righteous). The learned unanimously attest that these verses were revealed in honor of Mawlānā ʿAlī and his family, when they fasted for three days and gave the bread of their house to the poor, the needy, and the orphans:[^cite-20]

> ⟪quran 76:8-9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَيُطْعِمُونَ ٱلطَّعَامَ عَلَىٰ حُبِّهِۦ مِسْكِينًۭا وَيَتِيمًۭا وَأَسِيرًا ‎ ‏إِنَّمَا نُطْعِمُكُمْ لِوَجْهِ ٱللَّهِ لَا نُرِيدُ مِنكُمْ جَزَآءًۭ وَلَا شُكُورًا ‎⟫
> *And they give food, inspite of their love for it (or for the love of Him), to Miskin (poor), the orphan, and the captive, (Saying): "We feed you seeking Allah's Countenance only. We wish for no reward, nor thanks from you.*
> And they feed the needy, and the orphan, and the captive, out of love for Him. Whatever We feed you, it is only for the sake of Allah; it is not for us to take any retribution from you, nor to be grateful.
> — **Quran 76:8-9**

The more a person's deed is performed solely for Allah's sake, neither seeking praise nor fearing blame from any quarter, and the more an action is strengthened neither by external rewards nor weakened by external hardship, the more acceptable such action becomes. This relationship between *niyyah* and deed illuminates ʿAlī's statement that his heart dwells in heaven whilst his body acts in the world. It is noteworthy that worldly morality is characteristically volatile, waxing and waning with tangible results: when good comes, a person persists; when results fail to appear, he abandons the effort. The deed of one who keeps the Hereafter before his eyes, by contrast, is sustained by sincerity of intention alone. This does not mean that sincere intention exempts one from prolific action; rather, sincere intention means that whatever the outcome, one continues in good deeds, never tiring or ceasing. An action that falters under circumstances or diminishes to mere formality reveals a deficiency of true intention. Pure intention demands ceaseless and unwearied striving to fulfill one's purpose.

The just person never despairs, never abandons the struggle to establish justice. His aim is not to achieve some result through justice, but rather the spiritual realization of justice itself. He understands that his physical existence is bound to external circumstance and ultimately to divine pleasure. Yet such a person does not grow weary when results are withheld; his effort endures as steadfastly as he is assured of the permanence of divine blessings. His deeds are strengthened by the divine attribute of justice itself.

Jesus Christ observed that when the principles of justice are conceived apart from spirituality, personal idealism arises—an idealism vulnerable to external consequences, thus broken beneath the weight of difficulty and despair. But when spirituality interpenetrates justice, the indestructible attribute of divine justice sustains it and grants it the power of fulfillment. To the degree that a person's principles rest upon spiritual knowledge, despair cannot touch him in the face of tribulation. We find an exemplar in the biography of Amīr al-Muʾminīn (Prince of the Believers) himself:[^cite-21] when he ascended to the apparent caliphate, successive storms of war and rebellion arose, so that he could not implement all the principles and strategies he desired. Yet despite these trials, he never faltered, never grew disheartened or depressed, nor was there any want of effort and determination in establishing justice. He used to say that no deed is trivial if piety is bound to it. For piety separates despair from the pious person, since he remains ever conscious of the truth. This level of piety (taqwā / fear of Allah) becomes a path of escape from the world's injustices, as ʿAlī said: ⟪ar-quote:من یتق اللہ یجعل لہ مخرجا من الفتن وا نور من الظلم⟫ "Whoever fears Allah, Allah will make for him a way out from trials and light in darkness."

<!-- section 20 (id=3592, raw_sort=20): عبادت کی فضیلت -->

## The Excellence of Worship

We now turn to that section of your letter in which you describe the essence of all virtues: prayer. At the outset you counsel the ruler to fulfill the duties of prayer. Here you instruct Malik al-Ashtar that he should devote the finest portion of his time to the work of Allah, after he has completed all his administrative tasks; this devotion is the very act of worship (*ʿibāda*). Malik has been especially charged to purify his religion through obligatory acts of worship and to clarify his devotion. In purifying your religion, the purpose is to refine the substance of your relationship with Allah through worship—a relationship that exists between the soul and Allah alone, for the depth of this relationship marks the quality of all human virtue.

He says: "Know that every action of yours depends upon your worship." Worship here does not mean only the outward forms of bowing and prostration, but the inner sincerity that animates and sustains the outward deed. The sincerity, intensity, and fulfillment of prayer achieve its purpose. He urges: "Exert the strength of your nights and days for Allah's sake, and complete the deeds through which you draw near to Him, and perform them without fatigue, and take your body to its limits." The crucial word here is *qurb* (nearness), which one attains through the dedication that springs from the depths of the heart in the solitude of the night's darkness. All outward deeds are governed by the person's pure *niyyah* to surrender to Allah. When a person's inner life is suffused with the light of prayer, its rays shine forth also in outward life. For this reason he asked Malik to dedicate the best of his time to Allah—that is, every portion of the ruler's time is for Allah's sake, provided the intention behind the action is pure and people are benefited thereby. Then a person will see that the fountains of obligatory and supererogatory prayers spill forth and their effects emerge in the outward deeds of his life. The hadīth (tradition) of the Messenger of Allah expresses this beautiful truth:[^cite-22]
