> My servant does not draw near to Me through anything more beloved to Me than the obligatory duties. My servant continues to draw near to Me through supererogatory acts until I love him. When I love him, I am his hearing by which he hears, his sight by which he sees, his hand by which he grasps, and his feet by which he walks.

To see and act through Allah means to perceive things according to their reality, and then to act in accordance with that perception. In another sense, it is to establish justice—to keep things in their proper place. It is significant in this hadīth that both obligatory and supererogatory prayers are the cause of nearness to Allah, yet the station of divine action (*fāʿiliyyat al-ilāhiyya*) is reached through deeds of worship, not through prayer alone. As ʿAlī says, take your actions to the limits of your capacity. This demonstrates that there is no benefit in careless, mechanical worship. He likened a person who prays without *ijtihād* (rigorous striving) to one who shoots an arrow without a bow.

As noted earlier, in order to connect with Allah and realize *tawhīd* (divine unity), pure integration of the self is required. Prayer is the place where the profound dimensions of the human soul are unveiled, cultivated, and unified. Therefore, the fulfillment of prayer is not through tongue and body alone, but through the whole of soul and body. Allah says:

> ⟪quran 24:36⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا ٱسْمُهُۥ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ فِيهَا بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ ‎⟫
> *In houses (mosques), which Allah has ordered to be raised (to be cleaned, and to be honoured), in them His Name is glorified in the mornings and in the afternoons or the evenings,*
> In houses which Allah has commanded to be venerated and His name to be remembered therein, glorifying Him in the mornings and evenings.
> — **Quran 24:36**

Regarding nearness to Allah, ʿAlī said: "Verily, Allah has made remembrance a means for hearts, through which they hear when deaf and see when blind."[^cite-23] In every age there have been special servants of Allah to whom He speaks in their thoughts, conversing with them through the essence of their intellect. They scatter the light of Allah in their hearts, their hearing, and their sight, calling people to the remembrance (*dhikr*) of Allah's days.

The importance of *dhikr* is evident in your statement, through which consciousness of the truth is created. By *dhikr* you mean not merely the invocation of a particular divine name, but the perpetual awareness of Allah—the very essence of all worship, meditation, and reflection. The purpose is not simply to remember Allah or to chant His names, but to contemplate His divine realities (*ḥaqāʾiq ilāhiyya*) through the outward and inward manifestations of His divine attributes (*asmāʾ*). In another place, Mawlānā ʿAlī speaks of *dhikr*:

There are those who have embraced the remembrance of Allah in such a way that neither commerce nor livelihood diverts them from remembering Him. They spend the days of their lives in it. They exhort people to justice, and they themselves stand as living exemplars of justice—they themselves show people how things are kept in their proper place and explain the manner of keeping things in their proper place. Spirituality is not separate from action, but rather a connection to the moral depths that arise from the relationship—a relationship achieved through worship in general and through remembrance in particular. Just as it has been demonstrated that sincerity of *niyyah* is the essential substance, so now it is clear that sincerity in prayer—which takes the body to its limits—is paramount. If the attribute of justice belongs to the essence of Allah, then the closer a person draws to Allah through prayer and remembrance, the more just he becomes and the more he cultivates within himself positive capacities, spirituality, intellect, and virtue. Justice is both the cause of worship and its fruit. This elucidates the bond between worship and justice. Justice teaches us to keep things in their proper place. Therefore, justice toward Allah is fulfilled through prayer and remembrance, while justice toward oneself and others is the consequence of the nearness achieved through worship of Allah—and from this nearness all virtues are born.

Amīr al-Muʾminīn has emphasized the outward prayer and its root (*dhikr*). Plato taught that the highest knowledge is knowledge of goodness (*khair*), for from it are born all good and right things. If a person acquires all the knowledge of the world yet does not acquire knowledge of goodness, he has acquired nothing. He drew a comparison between virtue and the Sun, saying that what the Sun does for sight, goodness does for intellect and being.

Once, Zalib al-Yamānī asked ʿAlī: "O ʿAlī! Have you seen the object of your sincerity?" He replied: "If I had not seen him, I would not have worshipped him." The questioner asked: "How did you see him?" ʿAlī answered: "The eyes of flesh cannot see him; rather, the heart sees him through the truth of faith." From this utterance we understand the great importance of *dhikr*, for through it the heart is purified and clarified. However, *dhikr* does not refer to knowledge of outward forms; rather, it is knowledge of the Creator of these forms, described in Islam as the divine attribute *al-Muṣawwir* (the Shaper of Form). Yet this remembrance cannot be expressed in words like other sciences; it demands tireless worship and unceasing labor day and night. It is like a spark created by the friction of effort; but once this candle is lit, it never extinguishes and continues to nurture itself throughout one's life.

The essence of justice in Amīr al-Muʾminīn's letter is this: in order for any society to establish justice, it must understand these Islamic concepts not merely through intellect but also through the heart, for the heart is connected with inner realities and only the heart can perceive them through the light of Allah's favor. This is not possible without His compassion. The prophetic requirement of justice is that all components of human life—worship, morality, action—be harmonized together on the principle of *tawhīd*. The realm of ethics cannot be separated from the realm of spirituality, for in ʿAlī's view, true virtue is that which is intrinsic, strengthened, and directed toward truth. Therefore, these requirements of justice in the soul can only be created through worship whose spirituality flows from remembrance. Only this final analysis establishes that it is remembrance that sets the standard for human virtue.


<!-- section 21 (id=3602, raw_sort=21): ذکر اللہ -->

## Remembrance of Allah

Ali al-Hajwiri, the author of *Kashf al-Mahjoob*, writes of ʿAlī ibn Abī Ṭālib (may Allah ennoble his face) as one possessed of extraordinary spiritual distinction. He was the cousin of Muḥammad Muṣṭafā (peace be upon him), immersed in the turbulent depths of trials and engulfed by the flames of divine love. Among the chiefs of the purified ones (al-Asfiyya) and the friends of Allah (al-Awliyāʾ), he occupied a station of unmatched eminence. His mastery of the realities of the higher world was so complete that the great master Junayd declared: "ʿAlī is our master in the knowledge of principles."[^cite-24] As the Imam of all intellectual and practical domains, his understanding of this spiritual path was unsurpassed. The Sufis recognize such knowledge as a matter of foundational principle, and they understand its practice as the endurance of calamities in the way of Allah.

His forbearance amid trials reflects the celebrated utterance of the Commander of the Faithful, in which he declared his love for those whom the ignorant find alienated from themselves. What the Sufis cherish and the ignorant shun is worship—a devotion so rapt that all else save the Creator falls away from consciousness. It is a death in life, wherein one sacrifices the grandfather, the self, and all other preoccupations in the path of Allah's attention, destroying oneself utterly for the sake of the Truth.

The Arabic term *dhikr* (ذكر) carries profound resonance, admitting no adequate substitute in other languages. It encompasses remembrance, reflection, complaint, repetition, glorification (*tasbīḥ*), and recitation. It also signifies commemoration, declaration, praise, celebration, fame, greatness, honor, admonition, and warning. Allah Himself has designated the Qur'an as *dhikr*.[^cite-25]

Yet the most elegant definition emerges from the lexicon of al-Rāghib al-Iṣfahānī, who writes that remembrance is the faculty by which a person preserves knowledge and understanding. While memory refers to the past, remembrance refers to the present making-known. *Dhikr* denotes the arising of something in the consciousness and speech of a person. Thus are recognized two varieties of *dhikr*: the mention of the heart, and the mention of the tongue—and of these two, further distinctions emerge. There is the *dhikr* which admits error, having boundaries in time, and there is the *dhikr* which admits no error, enduring eternally. The remembrance of Allah becomes possible only through the presence of the heart.

The remembrance of Allah (dhikr Allāh) is a consciousness that absorbs the divine presence, yet it operates concurrently as a spiritual discipline. It is at once the end sought and the means of seeking—knowledge and the action flowing from knowledge. For the Sufis and the saints, *dhikr* is a systematic path through which the heart absorbs what the intellect comprehends, transforming abstract conceptual forms into concrete spiritual realities.[^cite-26] If prayer is the foundation of worship, then the remembrance of Allah surpasses it, as the Qur'an declares:

> ⟪quran 29:45⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱتْلُ مَآ أُوحِىَ إِلَيْكَ مِنَ ٱلْكِتَبِ وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ تَنْهَىٰ عَنِ ٱلْفَحْشَآءِ وَٱلْمُنكَرِ ۗ وَلَذِكْرُ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ مَا تَصْنَعُونَ ‎⟫
> Recite what has been revealed to you of the Book, and be steadfast in prayer. Indeed, prayer prevents indecency and evil, and the remembrance of Allah is greater; and Allah is Aware of what you do.

Numerous prophetic traditions (*aḥādīth*) extol the virtue of remembering Allah. The Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) once asked his Companions: "Shall I not tell you what is the purest of your deeds and highest in rank before your Lord, what surpasses the spending of gold and silver, and what is better than meeting your enemies in battle?" When they replied, "Yes, O Messenger of Allah, tell us," he answered: "It is your constant remembrance of Allah." The Commander of the Faithful similarly taught: "Remember Allah continuously, for it illuminates the hearts, and it is the noblest form of worship." Imam Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq (peace be upon him) confirmed: "Our Shīʿa are those who, when they are alone, often invoke Allah."

### Remembrance of Allah Strengthens Hearts

Let us now return to the sermon of the Commander of the Faithful, in which he declared that the remembrance of Allah is a burning (*ḥarq*) for the hearts. At the threshold of his address, he recited verses from the Qur'an of surpassing beauty:

> ⟪quran 24:35-37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ ٱللَّهُ نُورُ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ ۚ مَثَلُ نُورِهِۦ كَمِشْكَوٰةٍۢ فِيهَا مِصْبَاحٌ ۖ ٱلْمِصْبَاحُ فِى زُجَاجَةٍ ۖ ٱلزُّجَاجَةُ كَأَنَّهَا كَوْكَبٌۭ دُرِّىٌّۭ يُوقَدُ مِن شَجَرَةٍۢ مُّبَرَكَةٍۢ زَيْتُونَةٍۢ لَّا شَرْقِيَّةٍۢ وَلَا غَرْبِيَّةٍۢ يَكَادُ زَيْتُهَا يُضِىٓءُ وَلَوْ لَمْ تَمْسَسْهُ نَارٌۭ ۚ نُّورٌ عَلَىٰ نُورٍۢ ۗ يَهْدِى ٱللَّهُ لِنُورِهِۦ مَن يَشَآءُ ۚ وَيَضْرِبُ ٱللَّهُ ٱلْأَمْثَلَ لِلنَّاسِ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَىْءٍ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎ ‏فِى بُيُوتٍ أَذِنَ ٱللَّهُ أَن تُرْفَعَ وَيُذْكَرَ فِيهَا ٱسْمُهُۥ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ فِيهَا بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ ‎ ‏رِجَالٌۭ لَّا تُلْهِيهِمْ تِجَارَةٌۭ وَلَا بَيْعٌ عَن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ وَإِقَامِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةِ وَإِيتَآءِ ٱلزَّكَوٰةِ ۙ يَخَافُونَ يَوْمًۭا تَتَقَلَّبُ فِيهِ ٱلْقُلُوبُ وَٱلْأَبْصَرُ ‎⟫
> Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth, the likeness of His light is like a lamp in a niche, a lamp in a glass candle, a candle like a star shining like a pearl, illuminated by a blessed olive tree, neither to the east nor to the west. He wills to guide His light, and Allah sets forth parables for mankind, and Allah knows all things in houses which Allah has commanded to be raised and His name to be remembered therein. They fear a Day whereon hearts and eyes will overturn.

When he approached the verse concerning men whom trade and goods distract not from the remembrance of Allah, he expounded with words of luminous clarity: Allah has made the remembrance of Allah a polish (*dihān*) for the hearts, by means of which they hear when deaf, see when blind, and respond when they would resist. In every age, there have been servants of Allah to whom Allah has spoken through the wellspring of their thoughts and intellects. He disseminated the light of guidance through their hearing, their sight, and the illumination rising in their hearts, calling people to the days of remembrance of Allah. Among them is a chosen group who prefer the remembrance of Allah above all else in this world, so that trade and commerce do not divert them from *dhikr*. They consume their days in this remembrance, living as though they have already crossed into the Hereafter, present in this world yet dwelling in the world to come.[^cite-27]

The connection between the burning of hearts and the verse of light is manifest and clear. The hidden light of the hearts is revealed through the remembrance of Allah. The inner light of consciousness is illuminated by the external light of *dhikr*—⟪ar:نُور عَلَىٰ نُورٍ⟫, light upon light. When the heart is kindled by this radiance, its effect spreads throughout all the faculties, and they too become illuminated. This phenomenon explains the meaning at the heart of the saying—⟪ar:نُور عَلَىٰ نُورٍ⟫, light layered upon light. "Burning" (*ḥarq*) denotes cleansing, unveiling, and bringing into the open. Allah says in the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 92:1-2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلَّيْلِ إِذَا يَغْشَىٰ ‎ ‏وَٱلنَّهَارِ إِذَا تَجَلَّىٰ ‎⟫
> By the night when it envelops, and by the day when it brightens.

In this oath, Allah swears by the night as it overwhelms and obscures—that which appears anew after non-existence. And He swears by the day as it brightens and becomes manifest—that which becomes apparent after concealment. In another place He declares:

> ⟪quran 91:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱلنَّهَارِ إِذَا جَلَّىٰهَا ‎⟫
> And by the day when it illuminates it.

Thus through the remembrance of Allah, the consciousness dwelling in the depths of the heart is awakened and manifested in the form of deed. The role of the heart deserves careful consideration here: on one hand it receives the divine light through *dhikr*, reflecting it upon all other faculties; on the other, the remembrance of Allah awakens the hidden consciousness in its depths, which then reveals the truths. The Commander of the Faithful spoke of these buried treasures of intellect (⟪ar:دفائن العقول⟫), the hidden consciousness within.[^cite-28] Thus it becomes evident that the true purpose of *dhikr* is the purification of the heart—the commander of the body and the seat of true spiritual discernment.

Allah says:

> ⟪quran 7:179⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنَا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيرًۭا مِّنَ ٱلْجِنِّ وَٱلْإِنسِ ۖ لَهُمْ قُلُوبٌۭ لَّا يَفْقَهُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ أَعْيُنٌۭ لَّا يُبْصِرُونَ بِهَا وَلَهُمْ آذَانٌۭ لَّا يَسْمَعُونَ بِهَآ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ كَٱلْأَنْعَمِ بَلْ هُمْ أَضَلُّ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْغَفِلُونَ ‎⟫
> And We have created for Hell many of the jinn and men. They have hearts with which they do not understand, eyes with which they do not see, and ears with which they do not hear. They are like cattle; nay, they are further astray. It is they who are the heedless.

Here Allah employs the term "heedless" (*al-ghāfilūn*). The word "heedlessness" (*ghafla*) stands as the opposite of *dhikr*, which means to remember and to be awake. The verse that follows illuminates the mystical practice of remembrance:

> ⟪quran 7:180⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْأَسْمَآءُ ٱلْحُسْنَىٰ فَٱدْعُوهُ بِهَا ۖ وَذَرُوا۟ ٱلَّذِينَ يُلْحِدُونَ فِىٓ أَسْمَٓئِهِۦ ۚ سَيُجْزَوْنَ مَا كَانُوا۟ يَعْمَلُونَ ‎⟫
> And all the best names belong to Allah, so invoke Him by them, and leave those who blaspheme the names of Allah, lest they be recompensed for what they used to do.

In the verses that follow, the intimate bond between remembrance and the heart becomes pellucid:

> ⟪quran 13:28⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَتَطْمَىِٕنُّ قُلُوبُهُم بِذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۗ أَلَا بِذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ تَطْمَىِٕنُّ ٱلْقُلُوبُ ‎⟫
> Those who believe and whose hearts find solace in the remembrance of Allah. Hearts are comforted by the remembrance of Allah.

> ⟪quran 50:37⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ فِى ذَلِكَ لَذِكْرَىٰ لِمَن كَانَ لَهُۥ قَلْبٌ أَوْ أَلْقَى ٱلسَّمْعَ وَهُوَ شَهِيدٌۭ ‎⟫
> Surely in that is a lesson for him who possesses a heart, or he is attentive, and listens carefully.

> ⟪quran 8:2⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّمَا ٱلْمُؤْمِنُونَ ٱلَّذِينَ إِذَا ذُكِرَ ٱللَّهُ وَجِلَتْ قُلُوبُهُمْ وَإِذَا تُلِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ آيَتُهُۥ زَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَنًۭا وَعَلَىٰ رَبِّهِمْ يَتَوَكَّلُونَ ‎⟫
> The believers are only those whose hearts are filled with awe when Allah is mentioned, and when His verses are recited to them, their faith increases, and in their Lord they rely.

> ⟪quran 39:22⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَفَمَن شَرَحَ ٱللَّهُ صَدْرَهُۥ لِلْإِسْلَمِ فَهُوَ عَلَىٰ نُورٍۢ مِّن رَّبِّهِۦ ۚ فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْقَسِيَةِ قُلُوبُهُم مِّن ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ فِى ضَلَلٍۢ مُّبِينٍ ‎⟫
> Is he whose breast Allah has opened up to Islam, so that he is in a light from his Lord? Woe to those whose hearts are not affected by the remembrance of Allah. Those are in manifest error.

> ⟪quran 39:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱللَّهُ نَزَّلَ أَحْسَنَ ٱلْحَدِيثِ كِتَبًۭا مُّتَشَبِهًۭا مَّثَانِىَ تَقْشَعِرُّ مِنْهُ جُلُودُ ٱلَّذِينَ يَخْشَوْنَ رَبَّهُمْ ثُمَّ تَلِينُ جُلُودُهُمْ وَقُلُوبُهُمْ إِلَىٰ ذِكْرِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ذَلِكَ هُدَى ٱللَّهِ يَهْدِى بِهِۦ مَن يَشَآءُ ۚ وَمَن يُضْلِلِ ٱللَّهُ فَمَا لَهُۥ مِنْ هَادٍ ‎⟫
> Allah has sent down the best discourse, a Book continuous in its repetitions, whereupon the skins of those who fear their Lord shudder; then their skins and hearts soften to the remembrance of Allah. That is the guidance of Allah; He guides therewith whom He will, and whomever Allah leaves astray has no guide.

These verses demonstrate with crystalline clarity that remembrance of Allah is intimately bound to the heart, which renders consciousness into reality. The heart requires enrichment through the remembrance of Allah. The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) proclaimed: "For everything there is a polish (*dihān*), and the polish of the heart is the remembrance of Allah."[^cite-29] In this saying we recognize a systematic process uniting action with consciousness, echoing the prophetic instruction: "Worship Allah as though you see Him." On the one hand, *dhikr* serves the purification of thought and contemplation; on the other, it comprises regular actions assuming diverse forms—glorification (*tasbīḥ*), magnification (*tamjīd*), praise (*taḥmīd*), sanctification (*taqīs*), declaration of divine unity (*taḥlīl*), and invocation of Allah. These remove the rust of forgetfulness from the hearts. The Messenger of Allah has spoken of such people as those of remembrance (*dhikr*), saying: "Verily, there are angels of Allah who traverse the streets in search of the people of remembrance; and when they encounter them, they say to one another, 'Come to that which your hearts desire.'"[^cite-30]

If we now contemplate the spiritual vision (*baṣīra*) by which the heart sees through the remembrance of Allah—that which is purified by *dhikr* and revived by faith—we arrive at the teaching of the Commander of the Faithful. He speaks of vision obtained through inspiration (*ilhām*), a sight no less than the sight of Allah Himself. Elsewhere he declares the pure heart to be the place of seeing Allah: "Whoever purifies his heart shall see Allah." The nexus between purity of heart and remembrance is evident in his invocation: "Where are those whose deeds are pure for the sake of Allah alone, and who purify their hearts with the remembrance of Allah so that it becomes the seat of rest for Allah?" This utterance accords with the sacred hadith in which the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) related: "My servant ceases not to draw near unto Me through supererogatory works until I love him. And when I love him, I become his hearing by which he hears, his sight by which he sees, his hand by which he grasps, and his feet by which he walks."[^cite-31] 

Here human sensation and action become integrated into the realm of divine reality, whereupon the heart attains spiritual vision. When such a station is reached, the heart—the center of consciousness—transcends the material realm, and its inner essence becomes united with the Truth. It begins to see as Allah sees, and at the final station, to see Allah Himself.

Abū Ṭālib al-Makkī (a master among the Sufis) expounds that if it is indeed true that Allah enters into human feelings through human deeds, then the highest degree of spiritual consciousness would be that the vision of Allah—not merely the sight of Allah by the heart, but the sight of Allah *as* the sight of Allah—is achieved through the heart. The Commander of the Faithful explicates this philosophy, declaring: ⟪ar-quote:أعرف اللہ با اللہ⟫ "Acquire the knowledge of Allah through Allah." At this ultimate station, Allah is both Seer and Seen, as He Himself has said:

> ⟪quran 85:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَشَاهِدٍۢ وَمَشْهُودٍۢ ‎⟫
> And by the Day that is witnessed and by Him to whom they appear.

What is witnessed is the inner essence of human consciousness; what is seen is divine reality. In other words, a person's deepest faith makes Allah present everywhere and at all times, as the Commander of the Faithful proclaimed in his sermon: "By Your transcendence which envelops all things, by Your names which are the foundation of all things, by Your knowledge which encompasses all things, by the light of Your countenance through which all things are illuminated."

Nothing can endure without its foundation. The Name of Allah—or the totality of His names—provides that foundation. To perceive things aright is to perceive the divine attributes which alone are real; created things are but the material reflection and manifestation of these names. When the heart is cleansed by the remembrance of Allah, it finds Allah in all things. The existence of Allah in all created things is affirmed in the Qur'an from two perspectives—the divine and the human:

> ⟪quran 2:115⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْمَشْرِقُ وَٱلْمَغْرِبُ ۚ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا۟ فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ وَسِعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> To God belong the East and the West. Whichever way you turn, there is the Face of God. God is All-embracing, All-knowing.

> ⟪quran 41:53⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَتِنَا فِى ٱلأٓفَاقِ وَفِىٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ حَتَىٰ يَتَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُ ٱلْحَقُّ ۗ أَوَلَمْ يَكْفِ بِرَبِّكَ أَنَّهُۥ عَلَىٰ كُلِّ شَىْءٍۢ شَهِيدٌ ‎⟫
> We will show them Our signs in the world and in their own souls until it becomes clear to them that it is the truth. Is it not sufficient that their Lord is a witness over all things?

The heart purified by the remembrance of Allah beholds these signs everywhere and in all things; yet such vision does not entail that Allah is reduced to human sensible phenomena. The Commander of the Faithful teaches: "Allah is in all things, yet not through proximity; and He is apart from all things, yet not through separation."[^cite-32] The divine presence in created things does not arise from Allah's nearness to them, nor does it diminish divinity. Allah is infinitely nearer to us while we are infinitely farther from Him, as He declared:

> ⟪quran 50:16⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا ٱلْإِنسَنَ وَنَعْلَمُ مَا تُوَسْوِسُ بِهِۦ نَفْسُهُۥ ۖ وَنَحْنُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ حَبْلِ ٱلْوَرِيدِ ‎⟫
> And indeed We have created man, and We know what he whispers in his soul, and We are nearer to him than his jugular vein.

> ⟪quran 112:4⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَمْ يَكُن لَّهُۥ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌۢ ‎⟫
> And there is none equal to Him.

Nothing can remain apart from Allah, yet still it has no connection with Him. All objects in their existence are simultaneously entered and exited by divine reality. His presence in all things and with all things does not diminish His divinity; His separation from all creation does not remove Him from them. As the Commander of the Faithful teaches, Allah is One—not in terms of numerical quantity, but in the sense that He admits no peer. What is unique cannot be enumerated. To count Allah is to commit *shirk* (association). The Commander of the Faithful makes clear that no existence is possible without His existence. He alone is truly existent; all else is mere shadow. The radical vision of divine unity (*tawḥīd*), which excludes all otherness, reveals that every being except Allah is a false god, for each claims apparent oneness while standing opposed to the True Oneness of Allah.

All praise belongs to Allah—present in the hidden essence of things, whose essence manifests through the existence of creatures. The eye that sees cannot bear to gaze upon it; the eye that does not perceive cannot deny its reality; nor can the heart that acknowledges it witness it directly. He is so high that nothing surpasses Him, yet so near that nothing approaches Him. Allah has not equipped the intellect to fathom His attributes, yet He has not withheld them from knowledge.

Thus we encounter a paradox: on one hand, we cannot even grasp His attributes; on the other, knowledge of Him is possible. Through this paradox emerges another dimension of *dhikr*—to remember is to recognize. That is, the human being combines elements of knowledge already present in consciousness, yet forgotten. One recognizes what has been forgotten, and thus knows it again. This does not mean knowledge is fragmented and must be reassembled into a picture; rather, it is like awakening again after clouds of primordial forgetfulness have been dispersed.

In his first sermon, the Commander of the Faithful declares: ⟪ar-quote:اول الدین معرفتہ⟫ "The first principle of religion is its knowledge." The word "first" (*awwal*) may signify both "former" and "foundation." Knowledge here means not mere acquisition but *recognition* (*maʿrifa*). This reveals that Allah has already placed knowledge of the Truth in human consciousness. Through the remembrance of Allah, the human being recognizes this knowledge—recalling what was already known but had become obscured. In the same sermon, he declares:

⟪ar-quote:فَبَعَثَ فِيهمْ رُسُلَهُ، وَوَاتَرَ إِلَيْهِمْ أَنْبِياءَهُ، لِيَسْتَأْدُوهُمْ مِيثَاقَ فِطْرَتِهِ، وَيُذَكِّرُوهُمْ مَنْسِيَّ نِعْمَتِهِ، وَيَحْتَجُّوا عَلَيْهِمْ بَالتَّبْلِيغِ، وَيُثِيرُوا لَهُمْ دَفَائِنَ الْعُقُولِ، وَيُرُوهُمْ آيَاتِ الْمَقْدِرَةِ⟫

"Allah sent forth the Messengers from among them to exact the covenant of His creation (*fitra*), and to remind them of the blessings they had forgotten. He sent them to prove the case against them by revelation, to awaken for them the buried treasures of intellect (*dafāʾin al-ʿuqūl*), and to show them the signs of His power."[^cite-33]

These buried treasures are the knowledge which Allah has placed in the depths of human consciousness—the very knowledge to which Allah bore witness at the moment of creation, as He declares:

> ⟪quran 7:172⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِن ۢ بَنِىٓ آدَمَ مِن ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ وَأَشْهَدَهُمْ عَلَىٰٓ أَنفُسِهِمْ أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ ۖ قَالُوا۟ بَلَىٰ ۛ شَهِدْنَآ ۛ أَن تَقُولُوا۟ يَوْمَ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ إِنَّا كُنَّا عَنْ هَذَا غَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> And when your Lord brought forth from the Children of Adam from their loins, their offspring, and made them testify as to themselves: "Am I not your Lord?" they said: "Yes, we testify." Lest you should say on the Day of Resurrection: "We were not aware of this."

These divine realities may also be understood as the Divine Spirit which Allah breathed into Adam:

> ⟪quran 32:9⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ثُمَّ سَوَّىٰهُ وَنَفَخَ فِيهِ مِن رُّوحِهِۦ ۖ وَجَعَلَ لَكُمُ ٱلسَّمْعَ وَٱلْأَبْصَرَ وَٱلْأَفْـِٔدَةَ ۚ قَلِيلًۭا مَّا تَشْكُرُونَ ‎⟫
> Then He fashioned him and breathed into him of His spirit, and gave you hearing and sight and hearts. Little thanks do you give!

> ⟪quran 2:31⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ ٱلْأَسْمَآءَ كُلَّهَا ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى ٱلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ فَقَالَ أَنۢبِـُٔونِى بِأَسْمَآءِ هَٓؤُلَآءِ إِن كُنتُمْ صَدِقِينَ ‎⟫
> And Allah taught Adam all the names, then He presented them to the angels, and said: "Tell Me the names of these, if you are truthful."

> ⟪quran 30:30⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَأَقِمْ وَجْهَكَ لِلدِّينِ حَنِيفًۭا ۚ فِطْرَتَ ٱللَّهِ ٱلَّتِى فَطَرَ ٱلنَّاسَ عَلَيْهَا ۚ لَا تَبْدِيلَ لِخَلْقِ ٱللَّهِ ۚ ذَلِكَ ٱلدِّينُ ٱلْقَيِّمُ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَ ٱلنَّاسَ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫
> So set your face upright to the religion, the very natural disposition (*fitra*) with which Allah has created mankind. There is no alteration of the creation of Allah. That is the right religion, but most of the people do not know.

This demonstrates that the knowledge of Allah has been inscribed in the primordial nature (*fitra*) of humanity—the very nature from which Allah took witness at creation, as mentioned in the preceding verse. When asked about the divine nature, Imam al-Bāqir (peace be upon him) explained: Allah created all creatures upon divine unity (*tawḥīd*), such that they testified—"Allah is our Lord." This reveals that knowledge of Allah is the explication of human nature. Thus, as the Commander of the Faithful taught, the knowledge of Allah cannot be hidden from the human intellect.

Yet although this knowledge has been preserved eternally in the human intellect, it has been neglected—the precise inverse of the remembrance of Allah. This defect cannot be remedied by any measure of external learning alone. Only when the inner consciousness of remembrance wells up from the depths of the heart and unites with external revelation does this divine knowledge become transparent to the heart and intellect. The treasures of knowledge buried within the intellect then emerge.

The Commander of the Faithful declares: "Praise be to Allah, who is known without seeing."[^cite-34] Yet this statement harbors a profound paradox, intensified by his further utterance: "Through created things, the Creator becomes manifest to the intellect, and through created things, He is hidden from the eyes." Here speaks the veil (*ḥijāb*) born of creation. In a sense, all creatures themselves are veils, for they conceal the divine revelations within themselves while simultaneously witnessing to the existence of their Creator through their own existence. This is why he says: ⟪ar-quote:لا تحجبہ الحجب⟫ "No veil can hide Him." The veil is compelled to reveal what it conceals, for in revealing its own existence to the veil, the truth is made evident. The Master of the Universe teaches: ⟪ar-quote:لو کشف الغطاء ما ازدت یقینا⟫ "Were the veil lifted, my certainty would not increase."[^cite-35] Yet it can be seen by the heart purified through the remembrance of Allah—the heart that can now perceive after having been blind. Then he resolves the paradox: "The veil between Him and His creation is creation itself, in order that there might be distinction between Creator and creature, between the finite and the infinite, between the Lord and the one who is lorded over."

All creatures—all the veils brought forth by creation—exemplify the divine attribute of *al-Ẓāhir* (the Manifest), in that they are apparent, visible, clear, and disclosed. That is, they express the divine reality of creation itself. Allah manifests a portion of His hidden treasures as visible creation, displaying what is outward (⟪ar:الظاہر⟫, *al-Ẓāhir*) while concealing the inner mystery (⟪ar:الباطن⟫, *al-Bāṭin*). Therefore, the veil of creation is in fact the manifestation of the Creator. But what does this veil conceal? The divine unity (*Tawḥīd*) of Allah! For this is ⟪ar:الحق⟫ (*al-Ḥaqq*, the Truth)—the foundation of its essence and being. As noted before, the divine attributes of Allah form the ground of all creation. This proves that the foundation of all things is a single Truth. The essence of creation rests upon the divine attributes of the Truth. To associate a creature with Allah is to commit *shirk* (association with the divine). Therefore, the vision of divine unity protects us from this *shirk*. For this reason there must always remain a distinction between Creator and creature, between the finite and the infinite, between the Lord and the one who is lorded over.

The veil of creation guards nature against pantheism and against reducing Allah's infinite divinity to the limited forms of human understanding. Likewise, *tanzīh* (the transcendence of Allah from all attributes) and *tasbīḥ* (affirmation of His attributes) also serve as veils—yet veils perceived in the light of one another. Transcendence and immanence function as veils only insofar as these apparently opposing views are perceived in the spiritual vision of *tawḥīd*—the manifestation of the manifest and the non-manifestation of the unmanifest—wherein each illuminates the other. Unilateral emphasis on Allah's manifestation becomes a veil, for it conceals from us the inward aspect of His nature. Similarly, insistence on His inwardness alone becomes an obscuring veil, rendering us unable to perceive the manifestation (⟪ar:الظاهر⟫) of Allah present in the bosom of His universe. In other words, veils arise not only because of creation itself, but also because of the weakness and limitation of human concepts and the circumscribed manifestation of divine attributes within them. For this reason, the denial (*nafī*) of divine attributes becomes necessary. Through this negation, consciousness is enabled to understand divinity and to perceive beyond the veil that cannot conceal it.

When Abū Saʿīd al-Kharrāz (a master of the Sufis) was asked, "How did you come to know Allah?", he replied by observing that He joins opposites together (⟪ar:جَمعُہُ الضِّدَّین⟫). He then recited:

> ⟪quran 57:3⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هُوَ ٱلْأَوَّلُ وَٱلْآخِرُ وَٱلظَّهِرُ وَٱلْبَاطِنُ ۖ وَهُوَ بِكُلِّ شَىْءٍ عَلِيمٌ ‎⟫
> He is the First and the Last, the Outward and the Inward, and He has knowledge of all things.[^cite-36]

Spiritual intuition (*ilhām*) empowers a person to perceive apparently disparate objects as unified in the light of divine unity. At this profound level of consciousness, a transformative process commences: from it arises knowledge of the Truth, and the heart begins to behold Allah through the vision of the Truth itself. Only the divine realities can be magnified! Truths hidden in the depths of faith—these alone the heart that has received the remembrance of Allah can perceive and comprehend. These are the facts that vindicate the reality of the Divine.


<!-- section 22 (id=3603, raw_sort=22): ذکر اللہ عبادت کی معراج ہے -->

## Remembrance of God as the Pinnacle of Worship

God Most High declares in the Qurʾān:

> ⟪quran 76:25⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord every morning and afternoon.*

and again:

> ⟪quran 73:8⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكِرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ وَتَبَتَّلْ إِلَيْهِ تَبْتِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *And remember the Name of your Lord and devote yourself to Him with a complete devotion.*

These injunctions, repeated throughout Scripture, direct the believer toward remembrance (*dhikr*) as a practice undertaken in solitude, humility, and awe. The Qurʾān emphasizes both the manner and the measure of this remembrance: it must be constant, sincere, and inward. As stated in Surah al-ʿArāf:

> ⟪quran 7:205⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱذْكُر رَّبَّكَ فِى نَفْسِكَ تَضَرُّعًۭا وَخِيفَةًۭ وَدُونَ ٱلْجَهْرِ مِنَ ٱلْقَوْلِ بِٱلْغُدُوِّ وَٱلْآصَالِ وَلَا تَكُن مِّنَ ٱلْغَفِلِينَ ‎⟫
> *And remember your Lord in your heart, humble and fearful, and do not be of the heedless.*

The Prophet Muhammad and the Commander of the Faithful, ʿAlī ibn Abī Ṭālib, exemplified an intensity and frequency of remembrance that transcended ordinary devotion. In Surah al-Muzammil, God describes the Prophet's nocturnal devotion and then permits a moderation suited to human capacity, yet the principle remains unshaken: remembrance, along with prayer, almsgiving, and righteous action, constitutes the framework of spiritual life.[^cite-37]

To understand the significance of remembrance is to grasp the meaning of the Divine Names themselves. These Names are not human inventions or arbitrary designations; rather, God has chosen them for Himself. Ignorance of these Names constitutes a kind of spiritual negligence, as the Qurʾān warns:

> ⟪quran 58:19⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱسْتَحْوَذَ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلشَّيْطَنُ فَأَنسَىٰهُمْ ذِكْرَ ٱللَّهِ ۚ أُو۟لَٓئِكَ حِزْبُ ٱلشَّيْطَنِ ۚ‎⟫
> *Satan has overtaken them and made them forget the remembrance of God. They are the faction of Satan.*

The Commander of the Faithful taught: "He who loves a thing speaks of it with passion" (*man aḥabba shayʾan lahija bidhikrih*).[^cite-38] The term *lahij* carries a dual sense—to dedicate oneself and to repeat without cessation. Love and remembrance are thus inseparable: the tongue naturally gravitates toward that which the heart cherishes. The Prophet, upon him be peace, embodied this truth when he said in supplication, "My tongue has dedicated itself to Your remembrance" (*lahija bih lisānī min dhikrika*). In another invocation, he declared: "O Thou whose Name is medicine and whose remembrance is healing" (*yā man ismuhu dawāʾun wa dhikruhu shifāʾun*).[^cite-39]

Here, the Divine Name does not signify a mere word or label, as names are commonly understood among mortals. Rather, it represents a remedy for the disease of error that afflicts humanity from birth—a cure for the heedlessness that has become second nature to the human soul. Just as medicine must be administered and ingested to heal illness (mere contemplation of a medicine brings no benefit), the remembrance of God must be enacted through speech and heart. To speak God's Names, to invoke them constantly, to let the tongue be moistened perpetually by His remembrance—this is the active, living remembrance that the Prophet taught when he said to a man overwhelmed by the obligations of the Law: "Let your tongue always be moist with the remembrance of God."[^cite-40]

The Qurʾān reinforces this reality in unmistakable terms:

> ⟪quran 33:41-43⟫
> ⟪ar:‏يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ ٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ ذِكْرًۭا كَثِيرًۭا ‎ ‏وَسَبِّحُوهُ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًا ‎ ‏هُوَ ٱلَّذِى يُصَلِّى عَلَيْكُمْ وَمَلَٓئِكَتُهُۥ لِيُخْرِجَكُم مِّنَ ٱلظُّلُمَتِ إِلَى ٱلنُّورِۚ‎⟫
> *O you who believe! Remember God with abundant remembrance and glorify Him morning and evening. He it is Who bestows His peace upon you, and His angels likewise pray for you, that He might bring you forth from darkness into light.*

Observe in this verse the profound connection between remembrance, Divine praise, and salvation from darkness into light. The remembrance of the believers and the blessings that flow from God's attention to them are woven into a single spiritual transformation. God Himself declares:

> ⟪quran 2:152⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَٱذْكُرُونِىٓ أَذْكُرْكُمْ وَٱشْكُرُوا۟ لِى وَلَا تَكْفُرُونِ ‎⟫
> *Therefore remember Me; I will remember you. And be grateful to Me, and be not ungrateful.*

The exchange is mutual and reciprocal: human remembrance evokes Divine remembrance. The Commander of the Faithful taught that whoever remembers God experiences the quickening of the heart and the illumination of the inner substance (*lub*, the seat of understanding). This resonates with those verses addressing "people of substance" (*ūlī al-albāb*), as in:

> ⟪quran 3:190-191⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱخْتِلَفِ ٱلَّيْلِ وَٱلنَّهَارِ لَآيَتٍۢ لِّأُو۟لِى ٱلْأَلْبَبِ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ يَذْكُرُونَ ٱللَّهَ قِيَمًۭا وَقُعُودًۭا وَعَلَىٰ جُنُوبِهِمْ وَيَتَفَكَّرُونَ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ‎⟫
> *Verily, in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and in the alternation of night and day, are signs for people of substance—those who remember God standing, sitting, and lying on their sides, and who reflect upon the creation of the heavens and the earth.*

The Qurʾān here unveils the reciprocal relationship between remembrance and contemplation. When the heart is enlivened through *dhikr*, consciousness awakens and expands. Contemplation deepens. When love mingles with this contemplation—as it must, for love generates speech of the beloved—a circle of faith is completed, each element strengthening the other. The more one thinks with seriousness upon the Names of God, the more one perceives their beauty; the more one loves God, the more one invokes His Names; the more one remembers His Names, the more one penetrates the hidden meanings of the verses. Thus contemplation leads to increase in remembrance, and remembrance to increase in contemplation.

The remembrance of God stands as the zenith of all devotional acts. Unlike prayer, fasting, and pilgrimage—which require specific times, places, and prescribed forms—*dhikr* admits no such constraints. It may be performed at any hour, in any dwelling, in any circumstance. The Imam Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq, upon him be peace, taught: "Every act has a limit that, once reached, is concluded—save the remembrance of God. There is no terminus to it." God has indeed prescribed specific obligations for humankind; he who fulfills the fast during the month of Ramaḍān completes that obligation. But remembrance knows no such boundary. The Imam Muḥammad al-Bāqir, upon him be peace, would engage in remembrance whilst eating and whilst walking, integrating this supreme practice into the ordinary rhythms of life.

This principle is crystallized in the Qurʾānic description of those who transcend distraction:

> ⟪quran 70:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَلَىٰ صَلَاتِهِمْ دَآئِمُونَ ‎⟫
> *Those who remain constant in their prayer.*

Here, prayer itself becomes synonymous with the perpetual state of remembrance. God Himself establishes this equation:

> ⟪quran 20:14⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّنِىٓ أَنَا ٱللَّهُ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّآ أَنَا۠ فَٱعْبُدْنِى وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ لِذِكْرِىٓ ‎⟫
> *Verily, I am God. There is no god but I. So worship Me, and establish prayer for My remembrance.*

The Commander of the Faithful declared that ceaseless remembrance of God is the nourishment of the soul and the key to prayer itself. The Qurʾān establishes the hierarchy with precision:

> ⟪quran 29:45⟫
> ⟪ar:‏ٱتْلُ مَآ أُوحِىَ إِلَيْكَ مِنَ ٱلْكِتَبِ وَأَقِمِ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ ۖ إِنَّ ٱلصَّلَوٰةَ تَنْهَىٰ عَنِ ٱلْفَحْشَآءِ وَٱلْمُنكَرِ ۗ وَلَذِكْرُ ٱللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ۗ‎⟫
> *Recite what has been revealed to you of the Scripture, and establish prayer. Verily, prayer forbids indecency and wickedness; and the remembrance of God is greater.*

Prayer, though divinely mandated and essential, operates within prescribed boundaries of time, place, and form. It is a formality, yes, but also an inescapable necessity. It cannot be performed at all hours; it demands specific postures and utterances. Remembrance, by contrast, transcends such limitations. It is the living substance that quickens prayer itself, free from all constraints and impurities. The virtue of remembrance over prayer mirrors the superiority of the soul over the body: the soul does not negate the body, but encompasses it, animates it, and through that animation achieves perfection and wholeness.


<!-- section 23 (id=3604, raw_sort=23): ذکر اللہ کی حقیقت -->

## The Reality of the Remembrance of Allah

We turn now to consider the fruit of the remembrance of Allah—its essential purpose and deepest meaning—which is *taʾwīl* (realization), the process by which divine truth becomes actualized within human consciousness. This realization differs fundamentally from *tawḥīd* (monotheism), understood as union with the Divine; rather, it constitutes a process of self-integration, an assimilation of the self with itself, distinct from that union with another which monotheism entails.[^cite-41] We approach understanding this fruit through its contradiction: heedlessness, forgetfulness, distraction—the veils that obscure remembrance.

Allah condemns most severely the prayer born of hypocrisy, declaring:

> ⟪quran 107:4-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَوَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُصَلِّينَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ ‎ ‏ٱلَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَآءُونَ ‎⟫
> *So woe unto those performers of Salat (prayers) (hypocrites), Who delay their Salat (prayer) from their stated fixed times, Those who do good deeds only to be seen (of men),*
> — **Quran 107:4-6**

Woe, then, to those who pray while heedless of their prayers, who perform for show rather than sincerity. Similarly, Mawlā ʿAlī—the Commander of the Faithful—forbids the mention of Allah when accompanied by negligence and pretense. Yet paradoxically, when heedlessness is removed from remembrance itself, that remembrance becomes perfect: a state in which the person forgets even himself.[^cite-42] Here Mawlā ʿAlī holds together two seemingly contradictory imperatives—that negligence must have no place in *dhikr* (remembrance), and simultaneously, that such vigilant attention must be established that the self becomes oblivious, annihilated in the very act of remembrance.

He teaches thus:

> Do not mention Allah carelessly, nor forget Him in your distraction. Rather, remember Him in fullness—a remembrance wherein harmony reigns between your heart and your tongue, where what you conceal aligns with what you reveal. Yet know: you shall never truly remember Him until you become heedless of your own soul in this remembrance!

This teaching is the very essence of *al-taṣawwuf* (Sufism). It points to all the stations from which perfect sincerity—*al-ikhlāṣ*—emerges. Sufism bears the second name of *Ṣidq wa-l-Ikhlāṣ* (Truthfulness and Purity of Intention). On the one hand, *dhikr* enlivens the heart, generating that sincerity which is the virtue bringing perfection to remembrance itself; on the other hand, sincerity is precisely what perfects and completes the *dhikr*. In this perfected state, the utterance of the tongue stands in complete harmony with the intention of the heart—not the slightest divergence between word and inner purpose.[^cite-43] This accord between tongue and heart signifies that the divine reality released upon the tongue becomes the very echo of the heart's glorification, that heart being the mirror of the soul (*al-nafs*), the place from which all spiritual and moral excellences arise.

When the soul becomes entirely purified and transparent, unifying itself with both the intellect's utterances and the tongue's expression, it grows translucent to the spiritual standards—the divine realities—embedded within it. Then it begins to perceive the treasures concealed within its depths. These are the moral and spiritual standards that sparkle within the heart through the remembrance of Allah, only thereafter manifesting themselves as deeds. Without these inner standards, outward *dhikr* remains mere negligent formality, lacking all spiritual substance. The ignorant one is he who abandons the struggle for sincere remembrance, who turns from *al-jihād al-akbar* (the Greater Struggle—the struggle against the self) and neglects to fulfill Allah's commands.

Mawlā ʿAlī's teaching opens before us the door to the reality of *dhikr*, through which we may advance toward divine truth. This highest station requires *fanāʾ al-nafs* (the annihilation of the self), a revolutionary negligence of selfhood. For to perceive divine affiliation, one must remove the veil of self standing between truth and consciousness. The beginning of gnosis is self-effacement; its culmination is self-annihilation. Thus does the reality of *dhikr* demand this paradoxical negation. It shows that human movement proceeds from *kamāl awwal* (primary perfection) to the reality of divine truth, from human excellence toward *al-Ḥaqq* (the Real, the Divine Truth).

The first stage is the elimination of hypocrisy and the pursuit of sincerity, honesty, and integrity—virtues that produce human perfection. At this level, the person's individual identity remains intact. This harmony of intention and action constitutes *kamāl thānī* (secondary perfection), yet it is accomplished through the human being's own agency and thus ranks lower. In true remembrance, by contrast, the person's self-identity does not endure, for they have become oblivious to themselves. Here the focus shifts entirely from *al-dhākir* (the rememberer) to *al-madhkūr* (the Remembered One). The reality of *dhikr* becomes one with the Truth. At such a moment, one may say inwardly that it is Allah Himself who performs the remembrance, only appearing on the tongue of the human being. At this juncture, human existence becomes a deception that vanishes through self-annihilation.

In this light, we return to the prophetic *ḥadīth qudsī* (sacred hadith): "My servant ceases not to draw near to Me through supererogatory acts until I love him."[^cite-44] We now understand that by *Nawāfil* (supererogatory acts) is meant the remembrance of Allah. Noteworthy here is this: Allah is the source of every action of the *Dhākir* (the one remembering). Allah sees and hears the deeds of those whom He loves. Allah does not alter Himself to enter into a person's intentions and actions; rather, He becomes unified with that intention and action. In other words, divine realities cease to be obscured by the Dhākir's selfhood, enabling them to perceive beyond the suspicion of outward existence, and they begin to understand the inner realities of the Qur'an's verses:

> ⟪quran 37:96⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَٱللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *"While Allah has created you and what you make!"*
> — **Quran 37:96**

> ⟪quran 8:17⟫
> ⟪ar:‏فَلَمْ تَقْتُلُوهُمْ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ قَتَلَهُمْ ۚ وَمَا رَمَيْتَ إِذْ رَمَيْتَ وَلَكِنَّ ٱللَّهَ رَمَىٰ ۚ وَلِيُبْلِىَ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْهُ بَلَآءً حَسَنًا ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *You killed them not, but Allah killed them. And you (Muhammad PBUH) threw not when you did throw but Allah threw, that He might test the believers by a fair trial from Him. Verily, Allah is All-Hearer, All-Knower.*
> — **Quran 8:17**

The Prophet—peace and blessings upon him—and Mawlā ʿAlī illustrated this station of remembrance through a profound incident. During a battle, an arrow pierced ʿAlī's ankle. Yet when prayer commenced and he entered prostration, he instructed those present: "Remove this arrow while I am in prayer." They did so. When he rose from prayer and asked, "Have you withdrawn it?" his tone suggested he had been entirely unaware of the procedure. This marks the pinnacle of *dhikr*: the physical existence of the human being—all sensation related to it—has ceased to remain.

As the Messenger of Allah declared, "*Al-Iḥsān* (excellence, or spiritual realization) is to worship Allah as though you see Him, and if you do not see Him, know that He sees you." The Arabic phrasing of this *ḥadīth* is such that if one pauses at the correct juncture, the meaning transforms entirely: it becomes "If you do not see it, it sees you"—yet only Allah perceives the sight of Allah, never the servant. True manifestation of the Divine cannot be attained so long as any creature remains in view. In the account of Moses:

> ⟪quran 7:143⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَمَّا جَآءَ مُوسَىٰ لِمِيقَتِنَا وَكَلَّمَهُۥ رَبُّهُۥ قَالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِىٓ أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ ۚ قَالَ لَن تَرَىٰنِى وَلَكِنِ ٱنظُرْ إِلَى ٱلْجَبَلِ فَإِنِ ٱسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُۥ فَسَوْفَ تَرَىٰنِى ۚ فَلَمَّا تَجَلَّىٰ رَبُّهُۥ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُۥ دَكًّۭا وَخَرَّ مُوسَىٰ صَعِقًۭا ۚ فَلَمَّآ أَفَاقَ قَالَ سُبْحَنَكَ تُبْتُ إِلَيْكَ وَأَنَا۠ أَوَّلُ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ ‎⟫
> *And when Musa (Moses) came at the time and place appointed by Us, and his Lord spoke to him, he said: "O my Lord! Show me (Yourself), that I may look upon You." Allah said: "You cannot see Me, but look upon the mountain if it stands still in its place then you shall see Me." So when his Lord appeared to the mountain, He made it collapse to dust, and Musa (Moses) fell down unconscious. Then when he recovered his senses he said: "Glory be to You, I turn to You in repentance and I am the first of the believers."*
> — **Quran 7:143**

The radiance of *al-Ḥaqq's* brilliance rendered Moses unconscious. Allah did not manifest upon Moses but upon the mountain—a manifestation that human form could not bear.

Once, a companion of the Prophet—Abū al-Dardāʾ—observed ʿAlī lying motionless in a garden in Medina, his body utterly lifeless in appearance. Concerned, he hastened to the house of Fāṭima to inquire of her. She said, "My husband ʿAlī has not departed this life; rather, he must have swooned in the awe of Allah. Such states visit him often." Here *fear* denotes knowledge of Allah's greatness (*ʿaẓamah*). Allah mentions this fear as a mark of perfection in the Qur'an:

> ⟪quran 79:40-41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِۦ وَنَهَى ٱلنَّفْسَ عَنِ ٱلْهَوَىٰ ‎ ‏فَإِنَّ ٱلْجَنَّةَ هِىَ ٱلْمَأْوَىٰ ‎⟫
> *But as for him who feared standing before his Lord, and restrained himself from impure evil desires, and lusts. Verily, Paradise will be his abode.*
> — **Quran 79:40-41**

Though fear ordinarily terrifies, fear of Allah is beauteous, not dreadful. This fear grants one an attractive power toward divine truth. As the Sufis teach: when one fears a creature, one flees from it; but when one fears Allah, one runs toward Him. The Qur'an affirms this:

> ⟪quran 9:118⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَعَلَى ٱلثَّلَثَةِ ٱلَّذِينَ خُلِّفُوا۟ حَتَّىٰٓ إِذَا ضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ ٱلْأَرْضُ بِمَا رَحُبَتْ وَضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ أَنفُسُهُمْ وَظَنُّوٓا۟ أَن لَّا مَلْجَأَ مِنَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَّآ إِلَيْهِ ثُمَّ تَابَ عَلَيْهِمْ لِيَتُوبُوٓا۟ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ هُوَ ٱلتَّوَّابُ ٱلرَّحِيمُ ‎⟫
> *And (He did forgive also) the three [who did not join the Tabuk expedition (whom the Prophet PBUH)] left (i.e. he did not give his judgement in their case, and their case was suspended for Allah's Decision) till for them the earth, vast as it is, was straitened and their ownselves were straitened to them, and they perceived that there is no fleeing from Allah, and no refuge but with Him. Then, He accepted their repentance, that they might repent (unto Him). Verily, Allah is the One Who accepts repentance, Most Merciful.*
> — **Quran 9:118**

Mawlā ʿAlī's utterance testifies to his spiritual love and the union of his consciousness with divine truth—which is why Fāṭima, peace upon her, observed that such states visited him often.

The tradition teaches: "Surely Allah has a drink for His saints. When they drink it, they become intoxicated; intoxication brings them joy; joy brings them blessing; blessing brings dissolution; dissolution brings freedom; freedom brings purity. When they seek, they find; when they find, they attain; when they attain, they become unified with Him in such manner that no distinction remains between them and their Beloved."

The Messenger of Allah declared, "There have come upon them states of perfect *tawḥīd* (monotheism) that neither angel nor prophet can bear."[^cite-45] This feeling of monotheism is the fruit of all worship, the most intoxicating of all intoxications. The *Dhākir* is drinking this wine. In the initial stations, it appears that the servant drinks the wine of remembering Allah's names while engaged in remembrance; yet in the ultimate degrees, it is Allah Himself who drinks the wine of His servant's name and begins to mention it. This occurs when the person has destroyed the self in remembrance of Allah. Mawlā ʿAlī teaches that the remembrance of Allah is neither a matter of speech nor of thought. Rather, *al-madhkūr* (the Remembered) is first released, and *al-dhākir* (the rememberer) is released second—that is, Allah is first in remembrance, and human remembrance is but a reflection of divine remembrance, its very result. Allah declares: "Remember Me, and I will remember you."

Now, if we penetrate more deeply into *dhikr*, we perceive that the divine command released by the word *kun* ("Be!") through which all existence was created may itself be understood as remembrance. Allah called upon possibility by His name, thereby bringing it into existence from non-being. Allah was the remembrance of creation, and creation became His remembrance. The Qur'an questions us:

> ⟪quran 76:1⟫
> ⟪ar:‏هَلْ أَتَىٰ عَلَى ٱلْإِنسَنِ حِينٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلدَّهْرِ لَمْ يَكُن شَيْـًۭٔا مَّذْكُورًا ‎⟫
> *Has there not been over man a period of time, when he was nothing to be mentioned?*
> — **Quran 76:1**

Here humanity is called something that Allah brought into being. The mention of a time when there was no mention of it indicates a time when Allah had not yet commanded humanity's emergence from non-being. At that hour, though human beings existed in Allah's knowledge alone, they were known solely to Him. This signifies that Allah's remembrance of humanity precedes humanity's existence, and the mention of the Formless Divine supersedes human mention. Humanity mentions Allah through His names; Allah mentions humanity through the word *kun*. Yet this word was not uttered for a single moment only to fade. Rather, it continues to resonate within the human soul until the Day of Judgment, bearing witness to the divinity of Allah the Almighty. Through this word, Allah breathed into the soul the breath of existence itself.

Hazrat Kāmil once asked the Commander of the Faithful, "What is *al-Ḥaqīqah* (the Reality)?" He replied: "Reality is the name denoting the manifestation of Allah's glory, unmediated by any veil."[^cite-46] In the light of gnosis, the name of annihilation of *al-mahūm* (that which is feared) is Reality. The name of complete union with the attribute of *tawḥīd* is *al-Ḥaqīqah*. It is a light emanating from the dawn of eternity, whose rays illuminate the temple of monotheism—by "temple," referring to Allah in the station of unity. These are the names that give life to the soul and sustenance to it. The soul is the manifestation of the divine names, the place wherein Allah manifests Himself in particular modes. Ibn al-ʿArabī writes in his *Futūḥāt al-Makkiyyah*: "All praise belongs to Him who created things from nothingness and negated them, bringing them into existence through the attention of His words." As a result of the Divine Word's attention to possible objects, the realities of this world come into being. That is, the spirit of possibilities is breathed into existence, which is related to the body. The heart within this body is the name of Allah giving it life. Every servant has a name derived from his Master. Thus does the servant become the body of the Master, and the Master becomes the heart of the servant.

This example recalls Mawlā ʿAlī's saying that remembrance burns the hearts. The divine name descending from above reflects in the name resonating within the heart, and this reflection occurs when the rust of the heart is consumed by the burning of remembrance. It is the union of an outer light with an inner light, representing the Qur'anic verse of light: *Nūr ʿalā Nūr* ("Light upon light").

Now a question arises: What is the difference between the divine names, which are the origin of all things, and the names mentioned explicitly in the Qur'an? On one hand, all creation is the Book of Allah, and all manifestations are the words of this book; on the other hand, there are specific names mentioned in the Qur'an which we are commanded to glorify. Why this distinction? The Qur'an itself provides an answer:

> ⟪quran 17:110⟫
> ⟪ar:‏قُلِ ٱدْعُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ أَوِ ٱدْعُوا۟ ٱلرَّحْمَنَ ۖ أَيًّۭا مَّا تَدْعُوا۟ فَلَهُ ٱلْأَسْمَآءُ ٱلْحُسْنَىٰ ۚ وَلَا تَجْهَرْ بِصَلَاتِكَ وَلَا تُخَافِتْ بِهَا وَٱبْتَغِ بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ سَبِيلًۭا ‎⟫
> *Say (O Muhammad PBUH): "Invoke Allah or invoke the Most Beneficent (Allah), by whatever name you invoke Him (it is the same), for to Him belong the Best Names. And offer your Salat (prayer) neither aloud nor in a low voice, but follow a way between.*
> — **Quran 17:110**

In this verse, Allah Himself admonishes the believers to invoke the names revealed in the Qur'an—names altogether distinct from the idols:

> ⟪quran 53:23⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنْ هِىَ إِلَّآ أَسْمَآءٌۭ سَمَّيْتُمُوهَآ أَنتُمْ وَآبَآؤُكُم مَّآ أَنزَلَ ٱللَّهُ بِهَا مِن سُلْطَنٍ ۚ إِن يَتَّبِعُونَ إِلَّا ٱلظَّنَّ وَمَا تَهْوَى ٱلْأَنفُسُ ۖ وَلَقَدْ جَآءَهُم مِّن رَّبِّهِمُ ٱلْهُدَىٰٓ ‎⟫
> *They are but names which you have named, you and your fathers, for which Allah has sent down no authority. They follow but a guess and that which they themselves desire, whereas there has surely come to them the Guidance from their Lord!*
> — **Quran 53:23**

The names of idols are mere labels attached to worldly appearances, signs bearing no connection to actual reality. But Allah's names are intimately related to His manifestation; they are the very reality of the substances He created. Therefore, these names possess not merely the power to inform, but the transformative power to reshape. They possess the capacity to reveal Allah's greatness and reality within the human heart and intellect. For this reason, Allah's existence is inevitable—no existence lies outside the scope of His being. Yet rust upon the heart conceals His presence, though the heart itself is Allah's creation.

Therefore, one must purify the heart inwardly through remembrance of Allah, so that the inner reality may be unveiled. The divine names are the summit of manifestations, encompassing all appearances within themselves while remaining transcendent above them. This inner and outer reality may be likened to light and shadow: both are manifestations of one essence, yet bear no direct relation to one another. As Ibn al-ʿArabī teaches, the existence of *al-Ḥaqq* (the Real) is a fixed light, while all creation is the shadow following that light.

Mawlā ʿAlī declares in his prayers: "I call upon You by all the names You have chosen for Yourself." The fact that Allah Himself has named Himself testifies to the greatness and power of these names. He also teaches: "You shall never be able to mention Him until you forget yourselves in His remembrance." What, then, is meant by forgetting oneself and becoming oblivious to it? It is impossible for a conscious person to lose awareness of their existence during remembrance. Should one attempt to forget oneself, that very effort would prevent such obliviousness. We understand, therefore, that forgetting oneself here means directing complete attention to Allah's names such that no space remains in soul, spirit, intellect, or being where remembrance does not dwell—leaving no room for the self to occupy. This capacity for annihilation is obtained through Allah's grace when one strives to remove the rust obscuring the heart. This rust that deprives us of vision of Allah's Oneness—that unity which has no parallel. Allah tells His Prophet: "We shall teach you to recite, and you shall not forget":

> ⟪quran 87:6-7⟫
> ⟪ar:‏سَنُقْرِئُكَ فَلَا تَنسَىٰٓ ‎ ‏إِلَّا مَا شَآءَ ٱللَّهُ ۚ إِنَّهُۥ يَعْلَمُ ٱلْجَهْرَ وَمَا يَخْفَىٰ ‎⟫
> *We shall make you to recite (the Quran), so you (O Muhammad (Peace be upon him)) shall not forget (it), Except what Allah, may will, He knows what is apparent and what is hidden.*
> — **Quran 87:6-7**

And: "Remember your Lord when you forget":

> ⟪quran 18:24⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِلَّآ أَن يَشَآءَ ٱللَّهُ ۚ وَٱذْكُر رَّبَّكَ إِذَا نَسِيتَ وَقُلْ عَسَىٰٓ أَن يَهْدِيَنِ رَبِّى لِأَقْرَبَ مِنْ هَذَا رَشَدًۭا ‎⟫
> *Except (with the saying), "If Allah will!" And remember your Lord when you forget and say: "It may be that my Lord guides me unto a nearer way of truth than this."*
> — **Quran 18:24**

That is: when a person forgets all that is not Allah, then they become capable of remembering Allah. If Allah dwells in the palace of affirmation, then humanity dwells in the palace of negation standing in contrast. When this negation—this creatureliness—is itself negated, then complete affirmation of Allah emerges. Just as the negation of a negation produces affirmation.

The Creator of existence declares, "I am the death of death!" Rūmī, speaking of ʿAlī's teachings in his *al-Mas̄nawī*, describes it thus: "He said, 'I have drawn the sword for Allah's sake. I am Allah's servant, not enslaved to my body's commands. I am Allah's Lion, not the lion of desire! My deeds witness to my faith. In battle, I am Allah's sword, carried by Allah's hand. I have cast the burden of selfhood from my path. I have forgotten all save Allah. Allah is my sun; I am His reflection. I am the wise one! I am the veil between Allah and His creation. I am full of pearls of Oneness, like a sword adorned with jewels. I do not slay in war; rather, I give life in the Hereafter!'"

Allah's movement toward His servant becomes possible only after one negates one's existence. This negation is the nothingness from which Allah Almighty created existence. That is, Allah created humanity from non-being, and now humanity must destroy the self to find Allah. One negates one's existence by negating the substance that never truly existed (for human existence is contingent and exhaustible), and through this negation acknowledges what has eternally been:

> ⟪quran 55:26-27⟫
> ⟪ar:‏كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍۢ ‎ ‏وَيَبْقَىٰ وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ ‎⟫
> *Whatsoever is on it (the earth) will perish. And the Face of your Lord full of Majesty and Honour will abide forever.*
> — **Quran 55:26-27**

Every creature bears two aspects or "faces": the divine aspect, which is the reality of all things, and the mortal aspect, which passes away. Thus does Allah's Face—the immortal reality—constitute not only divinity but the reality existing within all things. Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 28:88⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلَا تَدْعُ مَعَ ٱللَّهِ إِلَهًا آخَرَ ۘ لَآ إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ۚ كُلُّ شَىْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُۥ ۚ لَهُ ٱلْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ‎⟫
> *And invoke not any other ilah (god) along with Allah, La ilaha illa Huwa (none has the right to be worshipped but He). Everything will perish save His Face. His is the Decision, and to Him you (all) shall be returned.*
> — **Quran 28:88**

Al-Ghazālī writes that creatures are not destroyed only when reaching a particular time or place; rather, they exist in a constant state of perdition—for everything save Allah is imperfect in its own essence. Through the Face of Allah, it receives its survival from the Almighty, which we perceive as existence. Its being does not emanate from itself but from the Face of God. Therefore, Allah's Face is reality, and all else is deception. He continues concerning the Sufis: "No power remains in them except the remembrance of Allah; they lack even the power to remember themselves." When one reaches this station, one inhabits simultaneously the place of annihilation and the place of survival. Yet even annihilation perishes—for the soul, oblivious to itself, neglects even awareness of its own annihilation. Should one possess consciousness of self-annihilation, one would possess consciousness of self.

Al-Qushayrī teaches that whoever has not tasted the solitude of annihilation cannot receive the sustenance of remembrance. Here, solitude refers to the soul's proximity to itself, manifesting as self-praise, appetite, and egoism. This closeness cannot be removed save through remembrance of Allah. This is the reality of *dhikr* which the Lord encapsulates thus: "Become oblivious to yourselves in the remembrance of Allah." Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 2:198⟫
> ⟪ar:‏لَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَن تَبْتَغُوا۟ فَضْلًۭا مِّن رَّبِّكُمْ ۚ فَإِذَآ أَفَضْتُم مِّنْ عَرَفَتٍۢ فَٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ عِندَ ٱلْمَشْعَرِ ٱلْحَرَامِ ۖ وَٱذْكُرُوهُ كَمَا هَدَىٰكُمْ وَإِن كُنتُم مِّن قَبْلِهِۦ لَمِنَ ٱلضَّآلِّينَ ‎⟫
> *There is no sin on you if you seek the Bounty of your Lord (during pilgrimage by trading, etc.). Then when you leave 'Arafat, remember Allah (by glorifying His Praises, i.e. prayers and invocations, etc.) at the Mash'ar-il-Haram. And remember Him (by invoking Allah for all good, etc.) as He has guided you, and verily, you were, before, of those who were astray.*
> — **Quran 2:198**

Here, guidance refers to elevation in the degree of remembrance. The first is remembrance of the tongue—*dhikr al-lisān*—which relates to the self. Then comes remembrance of the heart—*dhikr al-qalb*—relating to acts of worship that release Allah's grace. Then remembrance of the secret—*dhikr al-sirr*—relating to insight into worship, from which divine attributes' truths are unveiled. Then remembrance of the spirit—*dhikr al-rūḥ*—relating to contemplation of the Essence in light emanating from that sight. Then remembrance of the hidden—*dhikr al-khafī*—relating to the beauty of origin, wherein duality yet exists. Finally, remembrance of the original—*dhikr al-aṣlī*—relating to true vision wherein duality is transcended. Mawlā ʿAlī teaches:

> Do not abandon remembrance because you do not feel Allah's presence in it. Better for you not to find Him in your remembrance than to forget Him. He will lead you from heedlessness to prophecy, and from there to a remembrance wherein all save the Remembered vanishes. And it is not difficult for Allah to do so.

Ibn al-ʿAjībah writes in his *Ḥikam*: "The more one is destroyed in Allah's name, the more one errs in knowledge of the Original."[^cite-47] He states, "Allah's name is the joy of my heart and the coolness of my eyes." Yet any attribute is named, and true felicity ever comes from a thing's essence, not its name. Imam Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq, peace upon him, declared:

> Allah's name is separate from His Essence. Everything upon which His name appears is creation, hence separate from Allah. Everything that is described is creation, and the Creator cannot be comprehended within the limits of His creation's names. Allah possesses ninety-nine names. Were name and attribute one, each would be a god. Rather, Allah is He to Whom His names point; they are separate from Him and His creation.

Each name refers to an attribute on one hand and identifies that attribute, while on the other hand, the name possesses its own identity. For instance, *al-Raḥīm* (the Merciful), *al-Karīm* (the Generous), and *al-Sattār* (the Concealer) identify Allah, yet these names themselves have identities separate from one another. The very separation of these names from each other attests to their limitation. Though real in themselves, they become contingent and secondary in the sight of Allah, their rank before Him a "contingent reality." The true reality of all names returns to the Self, which is Allah. That is, from one perspective there exists distinction between name and attribute, yet from another they are one. In one sense, the name is nothing but a divine attribute of the attribute; in another, the name is what is uttered in words. For instance, *al-Raḥīm* has an origin which is mercy (*raḥma*), and *al-Karīm* has an origin which is generosity (*karam*). Thus, *al-Raḥīm* is the name of Mercy, and *al-Karīm* the name of Generosity—in which case name and attribute coincide.

The attributes disappear into the attribute because they become unified with it, possessing no independent existence; this is the reality of *tawḥīd*. After this knowledge, the formula of sincerity no longer remains as a statement, for all gods have merged into the essence of Allah and vanished. Its meaning is: "There is no reality but the Real Reality"—the Self. From this perspective, only *Allāh* remains, for Allah is the One without peer, and none may know Him save Allah Himself.

The Messenger of Allah—peace and blessings upon him—stands as the exemplar of the perfect human being. Mawlā ʿAlī declares, "We are the Most Beautiful Names of Allah,"[^cite-48] for he—peace and blessings upon him—is *al-ʿalāmah al-ʿuẓmā wa-āyātuh al-kubrā* (the Greatest Sign and His Greatest Verses). The Messenger said, "Whoever sees me has seen the truth." Thus do the Messenger, ʿAlī, and the Imams, peace upon them all, manifest these divine attributes to humanity in human physicality. These beings are mirrors in which divine attributes shine. The brighter the light of truth upon them, the brighter the reflection in this perfected humanity.

In the first sermon of *Nahj al-Balāghah*, Mawlā ʿAlī declares: "The perfection of sincerity is to purify it from all attributes, for every attribute bears witness to its own attributer."[^cite-49] Thus, whoever describes an attribute of Allah takes it as attribute of Allah; whoever deems it paired creates duality; whoever creates duality divides it into parts; whoever divides it lacks true knowledge of it.

When Mawlā ʿAlī states that purifying Allah from His attributes is *tawḥīd*, he does not mean these divine attributes do not exist, but rather denies the notion that they are autonomous, externally attached to the Real separately, or exist outside Allah's Essence, distinct from His very Self. Allah is He whose attributes are boundless. What is denied here is that the reality of any divine attribute can be captured in human imagination and language. If divine attributes are not separate from the Essence, and if Allah's Essence is eternal and unlimited, then the attributes too are infinite. When the Self cannot be comprehended, neither can the attributes.

In one sense, this acknowledges the attribute; in another, it denies it—acknowledging that attributes are not separate from the Self, while denying that these attributes can be incorporated into human thoughts and concepts. This is the relation between the human soul and divine truth. The human being is desolate, possessing no existence in itself, yet simultaneously not separated from the truth, becoming oblivious to self in worship. When the human ceases to exist, then Allah's existence alone remains. Though great contradiction appears here, it is the truth: the sense of the perfect existence of the Real connects with the feeling of the self's non-existence.

The Prophet, peace upon him, said, "On the Night of Ascension, I learned the true meaning of the names and saw them return to an object and essence. What I saw was *Masmi* (the names), and my existence was mine. My journey was in me, pointing to me, through which I came to know that I am a pure servant bearing not the slightest trace of divinity."

Similarly, when Mawlā ʿAlī describes his greatness in his sermons, he describes the greatness of Allah manifested through him. They are the embodiment of Allah's greatness, and His greatness is the highest standard of self-negation. When someone said to Imam Jaʿfar al-Ṣādiq, "You are arrogant!" he replied: "I am not arrogant, for greatness is only befitting to Allah. I have completely cleansed my self-field of arrogance, replacing it with Allah's greatness. As long as selfish pride exists, divine Greatness cannot dwell there; but when greatness comes through the existence of divine Greatness itself, then the divine attributes shine more brilliantly and swiftly upon the mirror of the self, made transparent by divine realities. And this radiance was created when I cleansed the dust of ego and selfish desire (*al-hawā*) from my heart's mirror."

Now let us return to the *ḥadīth qudsī*: "My servant draws near to Me through obligatory duties, which are most beloved to Me, and ceases not to approach My closeness through supererogatory acts until I love him. When I love him, I become his hearing with which he hears, his sight with which he sees, his hands with which he grasps, and his feet with which he walks."

Consider the paradox: on one hand, obligatory duties are most beloved to Allah in the person's sight; on the other, the servant's supererogatory acts are the reason for closeness to Allah, due to which Allah begins to love this servant—a love penetrating that person's senses and faculties, reflecting *tawḥīd*. This paradox dissolves when we understand that when Allah loves obligatory duties, He loves something appearing separate from His Essence. But when Allah loves His servant—the servant oblivious to self in remembrance—that servant is manifold, for they have become Allah's manifestation, having become one with Allah. Thus does the servant's love of Allah become Allah's love of Himself. Allah desires to know Himself; therefore He created this world. When a person negates the self in remembrance of Allah and knowledge of Allah, then Allah's command to know Himself is fulfilled.

Mawlā ʿAlī declares, "Knowledge flows from me, and no bird can soar to my height!" It flows from you because you have become one with knowledge's source. Allah declares:

> ⟪quran 76:5-6⟫
> ⟪ar:‏إِنَّ ٱلْأَبْرَارَ يَشْرَبُونَ مِن كَأْسٍۢ كَانَ مِزَاجُهَا كَافُورًا ‎ ‏عَيْنًۭا يَشْرَبُ بِهَا عِبَادُ ٱللَّهِ يُفَجِّرُونَهَا تَفْجِيرًۭا ‎⟫
> *Verily, the Abrar (pious, who fear Allah and avoid evil), shall drink a cup (of wine) mixed with water from a spring in Paradise called Kafur. A spring wherefrom the slaves of Allah will drink, causing it to gush forth abundantly.*
> — **Quran 76:5-6**

This camphor wine is in truth the Essence of Allah. The righteous increase its spring because it is camphor-wine itself—undivided, bearing no duality within it. Remembrance of Allah not only removes the heart's dust, giving it life, but by the grace of the Remembered One, erases duality's very name and trace. It purifies the heart from all *shirk* (association) and establishes *tawḥīd* (the principle of monotheism). To understand this reality is to negate all other apparent facts.

On one hand, one knows Allah through the very impossibility of knowing Him, as He lies beyond creation's veil; on the other, in remembrance, when the person becomes oblivious to self, the distinction between Creator and creature vanishes. Then the person's soul does not alter with anything else; rather, that self-state becomes a state of perdition. Its existence vanishes; only consciousness remains—consciousness belonging to nothing, attached to no entity. Then one reaches the station of *ʿĀrif billāh* (one who knows through Allah); otherwise one remains at *ʿārifah bi-Allāh* (knowledge of Allah). As Mawlā ʿAlī said, "Know Allah through Allah!" The purpose of remembrance is not merely to make one forget all save Allah, but to understand that naught exists but Allah. When the heart is illumined by remembrance, vision returns after blindness, hearing after deafness. Wherever one gazes, one perceives the Face of Allah:

> ⟪quran 2:115⟫
> ⟪ar:‏وَلِلَّهِ ٱلْمَشْرِقُ وَٱلْمَغْرِبُ ۚ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا۟ فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ ٱللَّهِ ۚ إِنَّ ٱللَّهَ وَسِيعٌ عَلِيمٌۭ ‎⟫
> *And to Allah belong the east and the west, so wherever you turn yourselves or your faces there is the Face of Allah (and He is High above, over His Throne). Surely! Allah is All-Sufficient for His creatures' needs, All-Knowing.*
> — **Quran 2:115**

> ⟪quran 24:41⟫
> ⟪ar:‏أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ ٱللَّهَ يُسَبِّحُ لَهُۥ مَن فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ وَٱلطَّيْرُ صَٓفَّتٍۢ ۖ كُلٌّۭ قَدْ عَلِمَ صَلَاتَهُۥ وَتَسْبِيحَهُۥ ۗ وَٱللَّهُ عَلِيمٌۢ بِمَا يَفْعَلُونَ ‎⟫
> *See you not (O Muhammad PBUH) that Allah, He it is Whom glorify whosoever is in the heavens and the earth, and the birds with wings out-spread (in their flight). Of each one He (Allah) knows indeed his Salat (prayer) and his glorification, [or everyone knows his Salat (prayer) and his glorification], and Allah is All-Aware of what they do.*
> — **Quran 24:41**

In his sermons, the Commander of the Faithful proclaims: "I am the sign of Allah the Almighty! I know the secrets of God! I am the limit of all limits!
